<p><b>Jakarta</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/dÊ/: 'j' in 'jam'">dÊ</span><span title="/É/: 'a' in 'about'">É</span><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ÉËr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ÉËr</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/É/: 'a' in 'about'">É</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Indonesian pronunciation:Â </small><span class="IPA" lang="id-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Malay" title="Help:IPA/Malay">[dÊaËkarta]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Id-Jakarta.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ca/Id-Jakarta.ogg" title="Id-Jakarta.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>), officially the <b>Special Capital Region of Jakarta</b> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <i lang="id">Daerah Khusus Ibukota Jakarta</i>), is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indonesian_cities_by_population" title="List of Indonesian cities by population">Largest City</a> of <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. Lying on the northwest coast of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_population" title="List of islands by population">most populous island</a>, Jakarta is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_ASEAN_by_population" title="List of cities in ASEAN by population">largest city</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and serves as the diplomatic capital of <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>.
</p><p>The city is the centre of the economy, culture, and politics of Indonesia. It has a <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">province</a> level status which has a population of 10,609,681 as of mid 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Badan_Pusat_Statistik_2022_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Badan_Pusat_Statistik_2022-2">[2]</a></sup> Although Jakarta extends over only 664.01Â km<sup>2</sup> (256.38Â sqÂ mi), and thus has the smallest area of any <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">Indonesian province</a>, its <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_metropolitan_area" title="Jakarta metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> covers 9,957.08Â km<sup>2</sup> (3,844.45Â sqÂ mi), which includes the satellite cities <a href="/wiki/Bogor" title="Bogor">Bogor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Depok" title="Depok">Depok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tangerang" title="Tangerang">Tangerang</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Tangerang" title="South Tangerang">South Tangerang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bekasi" title="Bekasi">Bekasi</a>, and has an estimated population of 35Â million as of 2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Indonesia" title="List of metropolitan areas in Indonesia">largest urban area in Indonesia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities" title="List of largest cities">second-largest in the world</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Tokyo</a>). Jakarta ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indonesian_provinces_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of Indonesian provinces by Human Development Index">first among the Indonesian provinces</a> in <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">human development index</a>. Jakarta's business opportunities, and its ability to offer a potentially higher <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a> than is available in other parts of the country, have attracted migrants from across the Indonesian archipelago, making it a melting pot of numerous cultures.
</p><p>Jakarta is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_continuously_inhabited_cities" title="List of oldest continuously inhabited cities">oldest continuously inhabited cities in Southeast Asia</a>. Established in the fourth century as <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kelapa" title="Sunda Kelapa">Sunda Kelapa</a>, the city became an important trading port for the <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kingdom" title="Sunda Kingdom">Sunda Kingdom</a>. At one time, it was the <i>de facto</i> capital of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>, when it was known as <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a>. Jakarta was officially a city within <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a> until 1960, when its official status was changed to a <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">province</a> with <a href="/wiki/Capital_districts_and_territories#Indonesia" title="Capital districts and territories">special capital region</a> distinction. As a province, its government consists of five administrative cities and one <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Islands_(Indonesia)" title="Thousand Islands (Indonesia)">administrative regency</a>. Jakarta is an <a href="/wiki/Global_city#GaWC_study" title="Global city">alpha world city</a> and is the seat of the ASEAN secretariat, Financial institutions such as the <a href="/wiki/Bank_Indonesia" title="Bank Indonesia">Bank of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_Stock_Exchange" title="Indonesia Stock Exchange">Indonesia Stock Exchange</a>, and corporate headquarters of numerous <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Indonesia" title="List of companies of Indonesia">Indonesian companies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporations</a> are located in the city. In 2017, the city's <a href="/wiki/Gross_regional_product" title="Gross regional product">GRP</a> PPP was estimated at US$483.4Â billion.
</p><p>Jakarta's primary challenges include rapid urban growth, ecological breakdown, gridlocked traffic, congestion, and <a href="/wiki/Floods_in_Jakarta" title="Floods in Jakarta">flooding</a>. Jakarta is sinking up to 17Â cm (6.7Â inches) per year, which, coupled with the <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">rising of sea levels</a>, has made the city more prone to flooding. It is one of the fastest-sinking capitals in the world. Because of these challenges, in August 2019, President <a href="/wiki/Joko_Widodo" title="Joko Widodo">Joko Widodo</a> announced that the capital of Indonesia <a href="/wiki/Capital_of_Indonesia#Move_to_Nusantara" title="Capital of Indonesia">would be moved</a> from Jakarta to the planned city of <a href="/wiki/Nusantara_(planned_city)" title="Nusantara (planned city)">Nusantara</a>, in the province of <a href="/wiki/East_Kalimantan" title="East Kalimantan">East Kalimantan</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Replica_of_the_Luso-Sundanese_Padr%C3%A3o_Monument_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Replica_of_the_Luso-Sundanese_Padr%C3%A3o_Monument_2.jpg/170px-Replica_of_the_Luso-Sundanese_Padr%C3%A3o_Monument_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Replica_of_the_Luso-Sundanese_Padr%C3%A3o_Monument_2.jpg/255px-Replica_of_the_Luso-Sundanese_Padr%C3%A3o_Monument_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Replica_of_the_Luso-Sundanese_Padr%C3%A3o_Monument_2.jpg/340px-Replica_of_the_Luso-Sundanese_Padr%C3%A3o_Monument_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Replica_of_the_Luso-Sundanese_Padr%C3%A3o_Monument_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Replica of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luso_Sundanese_padr%C3%A3o" title="Luso Sundanese padrÃ£o"><i>PadrÃ£o</i> of Sunda Kalapa</a> (1522), a stone pillar with a <a href="/wiki/Cross" title="Cross">cross</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_Christ_(Portugal)" title="Order of Christ (Portugal)">Order of Christ</a> commemorating a treaty between the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Indonesia" title="Hinduism in Indonesia">Hindu</a> <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kingdom" title="Sunda Kingdom">Sunda Kingdom</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_History_Museum" title="Jakarta History Museum">Jakarta History Museum</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Jakarta has been home to multiple <a href="/wiki/Human_settlement" title="Human settlement">settlements</a>. Below is the list of names used during its existence.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kelapa" title="Sunda Kelapa">Sunda Kelapa</a> (397â1527)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jayakarta" title="Jayakarta">Jayakarta</a> (1527â1619)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> (1619â1942)</li>
<li>Djakarta (1942â1972)</li>
<li>Jakarta (1972âpresent)</li></ul>
<p>The name 'Jakarta' is derived from the word <i>Jayakarta</i> (<a href="/wiki/Devanagari" title="Devanagari">Devanagari</a>: à¤à¤¯à¤à¤°à¥à¤¤) which is ultimately derived from the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> à¤à¤¯ <i>jaya</i> (victorious),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and à¤à¥à¤¤ <i>krta</i> (accomplished, acquired),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> thus <i>Jayakarta</i> translates as 'victorious deed', 'complete act' or 'complete victory'. It was named after Muslim troops of <a href="/wiki/Fatahillah" title="Fatahillah">Fatahillah</a> successfully defeated and drove out the Portuguese away from the city in 1527.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jakarta-news-2011_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-jakarta-news-2011-8">[8]</a></sup> Before it was called Jayakarta, the city was known as 'Sunda Kelapa'. <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A9_Pires" title="TomÃ© Pires">TomÃ© Pires</a>, a Portuguese apothecary during his journey to <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>, wrote the city name on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suma_Oriental" title="Suma Oriental">his magnum opus</a> as <i>Jacatra</i> or <i>Jacarta</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECortesÃ£o199027â32_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECortesÃ£o199027â32-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 17th century, the city was known as <span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Koningin van het Oosten</i></span> (Queen of the Orient), a name that was given for the urban beauty of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kota,_Jakarta" title="Kota, Jakarta">downtown Batavia's</a> <a href="/wiki/Gracht" title="Gracht">canals</a>, mansions and ordered city layout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKampen1831291_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKampen1831291-10">[10]</a></sup> After expanding to the south in the 19th century, this nickname came to be more associated with the suburbs (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Menteng" title="Menteng">Menteng</a> and the area around <a href="/wiki/Merdeka_Square,_Jakarta" title="Merdeka Square, Jakarta">Merdeka Square</a>), with their wide lanes, green spaces and villas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Japanese occupation of the Dutch East Indies">Japanese occupation</a>, the city was renamed as <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn"><i>Jakaruta Tokubetsu-shi</i></i></span><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">ã¸ã£ã«ã«ã¿ç¹å¥å¸</span></span>, Jakarta Special City)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>The official name used is <span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Daerah Khusus Ibukota Jakarta</i></span>, which literally means <b>Jakarta Special Capital Region</b>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Jakarta" title="History of Jakarta">History of Jakarta</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Jakarta" title="Timeline of Jakarta">Timeline of Jakarta</a>.</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Precolonial_era">Precolonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Precolonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kelapa" title="Sunda Kelapa">Sunda Kelapa</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prasasti_tugu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="480" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Prasasti_tugu.jpg/170px-Prasasti_tugu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Prasasti_tugu.jpg/255px-Prasasti_tugu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Prasasti_tugu.jpg/340px-Prasasti_tugu.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prasasti_tugu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 5th-century <a href="/wiki/Tugu_inscription" title="Tugu inscription">Tugu inscription</a> discovered in Tugu district, North Jakarta</div></div></div>
<p>The north coast area of western Java including Jakarta was the location of prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Buni_culture" title="Buni culture">Buni culture</a> that flourished from 400 BC to 100 AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZahorka2007?_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZahorka2007?-13">[13]</a></sup> The area in and around modern Jakarta was part of the 4th-century <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Tarumanagara" title="Tarumanagara">Tarumanagara</a>, one of the oldest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> kingdoms in Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAyatrohaÃ©di2005?_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAyatrohaÃ©di2005?-14">[14]</a></sup> The area of <a href="/wiki/North_Jakarta" title="North Jakarta">North Jakarta</a> around <a href="/wiki/Kampung_Tugu" title="Kampung Tugu">Tugu</a> became a populated settlement in the early 5th century. The <a href="/wiki/Tugu_inscription" title="Tugu inscription">Tugu inscription</a> (probably written around 417 AD) discovered in Batutumbuh hamlet, Tugu village, <a href="/wiki/Koja,_Jakarta" title="Koja, Jakarta">Koja</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Jakarta" title="North Jakarta">North Jakarta</a>, mentions that King <a href="/wiki/Purnawarman" title="Purnawarman">Purnawarman</a> of Tarumanagara undertook hydraulic projects; the irrigation and water drainage project of the Chandrabhaga river and the Gomati river near his capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHellmanThynellVoorst2018182_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHellmanThynellVoorst2018182-15">[15]</a></sup> Following the decline of <a href="/wiki/Tarumanagara" title="Tarumanagara">Tarumanagara</a>, its territories, including the Jakarta area, became part of the Hindu <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kingdom" title="Sunda Kingdom">Kingdom of Sunda</a>. From the 7th to the early 13th century, the port of Sunda was under the <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a> maritime empire. According to the Chinese source, <i><a href="/wiki/Zhu_Fan_Zhi" title="Zhu Fan Zhi">Chu-fan-chi</a></i>, written circa 1225, <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Rukuo" title="Zhao Rukuo">Chou Ju-kua</a> reported in the early 13th century that Srivijaya still ruled Sumatra, the Malay peninsula and western Java (<a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kingdom" title="Sunda Kingdom">Sunda</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBungeVreeland19833_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBungeVreeland19833-16">[16]</a></sup> The source says the port of Sunda as strategic and thriving, mentioning <a href="/wiki/Black_pepper" title="Black pepper">pepper</a> from Sunda as among the best in quality. The people worked in agriculture, and their houses were built on wooden piles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAyatrohaÃ©di200560_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAyatrohaÃ©di200560-17">[17]</a></sup> The harbour area became known as <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kelapa" title="Sunda Kelapa">Sunda Kelapa</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Sundanese_language" title="Sundanese language">Sundanese</a>: <span lang="su" style="font-family:'Noto Sans Sundanese', 'Sundanese Unicode 2013'; font-size:;">á®á®¥á®á®ªá® á®á®¨á®á®</span>) and by the 14th century, it was an important trading port for the Sunda Kingdom.
</p><p>The first European fleet, four Portuguese ships from <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a>, arrived in 1513 while looking for a route for spices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeuken1999?_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeuken1999?-18">[18]</a></sup> The Sunda Kingdom <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luso_Sundanese_padr%C3%A3o" title="Luso Sundanese padrÃ£o">made an alliance treaty</a> with the Portuguese by allowing them to build a port in 1522 to defend against the rising power of <a href="/wiki/Demak_Sultanate" title="Demak Sultanate">Demak Sultanate</a> from central Java.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jakarta-news-2011_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-jakarta-news-2011-8">[8]</a></sup> In 1527, <a href="/wiki/Fatahillah" title="Fatahillah">Fatahillah</a>, a Javanese general from Demak attacked and conquered Sunda Kelapa, driving out the Portuguese. Sunda Kelapa was renamed Jayakarta,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jakarta-news-2011_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-jakarta-news-2011-8">[8]</a></sup> and became a fiefdom of the <a href="/wiki/Banten_Sultanate" title="Banten Sultanate">Banten Sultanate</a>, which became a major Southeast Asian trading centre.
</p><p>Through the relationship with Prince Jayawikarta of <a href="/wiki/Banten_Sultanate" title="Banten Sultanate">Banten Sultanate</a>, Dutch ships arrived in 1596. In 1602, the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>'s first voyage, commanded by Sir <a href="/wiki/James_Lancaster" title="James Lancaster">James Lancaster</a>, arrived in <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a> and sailed on to <a href="/wiki/Banten" title="Banten">Banten</a> where they were allowed to build a trading post. This site became the centre of British trade in the Indonesian archipelago until 1682.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs1981?_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs1981?-19">[19]</a></sup> Jayawikarta is thought to have made trading connections with the British merchants, rivals of the Dutch, by allowing them to build houses directly across from the Dutch buildings in 1615.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeuken1999?_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeuken1999?-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia, Dutch East Indies</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_colonial_buildings_and_structures_in_Jakarta" title="List of colonial buildings and structures in Jakarta">List of colonial buildings and structures in Jakarta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_De_stad_Batavia_TMnr_3728-537_(flopped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1416" data-file-width="2265" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_De_stad_Batavia_TMnr_3728-537_%28flopped%29.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_De_stad_Batavia_TMnr_3728-537_%28flopped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_De_stad_Batavia_TMnr_3728-537_%28flopped%29.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_De_stad_Batavia_TMnr_3728-537_%28flopped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_De_stad_Batavia_TMnr_3728-537_%28flopped%29.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_De_stad_Batavia_TMnr_3728-537_%28flopped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_De_stad_Batavia_TMnr_3728-537_(flopped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> around 1780</div></div></div>
<p>When relations between Prince Jayawikarta and the Dutch deteriorated, his soldiers attacked the Dutch fortress. His army and the British, however, were defeated by the Dutch, in part owing to the timely arrival of <a href="/wiki/Jan_Pieterszoon_Coen" title="Jan Pieterszoon Coen">Jan Pieterszoon Coen</a>. The Dutch burned the British fort and forced them to retreat on their ships. The victory consolidated Dutch power, and they renamed the city <i>Batavia</i> in 1619.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Batavia_-_Townhall_1770.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="339" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Batavia_-_Townhall_1770.jpg/220px-Batavia_-_Townhall_1770.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Batavia_-_Townhall_1770.jpg/330px-Batavia_-_Townhall_1770.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Batavia_-_Townhall_1770.jpg/440px-Batavia_-_Townhall_1770.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Batavia_-_Townhall_1770.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The City Hall of Batavia (<i>Stadhuis van Batavia</i>), the seat of the governor-general of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">VOC</a> in the late 18th century by <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Rach" title="Johannes Rach">Johannes Rach</a> c. 1770. The building now houses the <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_History_Museum" title="Jakarta History Museum">Jakarta History Museum</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jakarta_Old_Town" title="Jakarta Old Town">Jakarta Old Town</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Commercial opportunities in the city attracted native and especially Chinese and Arab immigrants. This sudden population increase created burdens on the city. Tensions grew as the colonial government tried to restrict Chinese migration through deportations. Following a revolt, 5,000 Chinese were <a href="/wiki/1740_Batavia_massacre" title="1740 Batavia massacre">massacred</a> by the Dutch and natives on 9 October 1740, and the following year, Chinese inhabitants were moved to <a href="/wiki/Glodok" title="Glodok">Glodok</a> outside the city walls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitton2003138â39_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitton2003138â39-20">[20]</a></sup> At the beginning of the 19th century, around 400 Arabs and Moors lived in Batavia, a number that changed little during the following decades. Among the commodities traded were fabrics, mainly imported cotton, <i><a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">batik</a></i> and clothing worn by Arab communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENasGrijns2000145_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENasGrijns2000145-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city began to expand further south as epidemics in 1835 and 1870 forced residents to move away from the port. The <i>Koningsplein</i>, now <a href="/wiki/Merdeka_Square,_Jakarta" title="Merdeka Square, Jakarta">Merdeka Square</a> was completed in 1818, the housing park of <a href="/wiki/Menteng" title="Menteng">Menteng</a> was started in 1913,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kebayoran_Baru" title="Kebayoran Baru">Kebayoran Baru</a> was the last Dutch-built residential area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitton2003138â39_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitton2003138â39-20">[20]</a></sup> By 1930, Batavia had more than 500,000 inhabitants,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenderson197081â82_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenderson197081â82-23">[23]</a></sup> including 37,067 Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBakkerKooyShofianiMartijn20081891_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBakkerKooyShofianiMartijn20081891-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 March 1942, the Japanese wrested <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> from Dutch control, and the city was named Jakarta (Jakarta Special City<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">ã¸ã£ã«ã«ã¿ç¹å¥å¸</span></span>, <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Jakaruta tokubetsu-shi</i></span><span style="margin-left:.09em">)</span></span>, under the special status that was assigned to the city). After the war, the Dutch name Batavia was internationally recognised until full Indonesian independence on 27 December 1949. The city, now renamed Jakarta, was officially proclaimed the national capital of Indonesia.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_era">Independence era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Independence era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MonasConstruction2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="937" data-file-width="630" decoding="async" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/MonasConstruction2.jpg/170px-MonasConstruction2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/MonasConstruction2.jpg/255px-MonasConstruction2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/MonasConstruction2.jpg/340px-MonasConstruction2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MonasConstruction2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the most monumental projects launched by Sukarno was the demolition of government buildings in <a href="/wiki/Merdeka_Square,_Jakarta" title="Merdeka Square, Jakarta">Merdeka Square</a> to make way for the <a href="/wiki/National_Monument_(Indonesia)" title="National Monument (Indonesia)">National Monument</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>After World War II ended, Indonesian nationalists declared independence on 17 August 1945,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaworoentoe2013_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaworoentoe2013-25">[25]</a></sup> and the government of Jakarta City was changed into the Jakarta National Administration in the following month. During the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">Indonesian National Revolution</a>, Indonesian Republicans withdrew from <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a>-occupied Jakarta and established their capital in <a href="/wiki/Yogyakarta" title="Yogyakarta">Yogyakarta</a>.
</p><p>After securing full independence, Jakarta again became the national capital in 1950.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitton2003138â39_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitton2003138â39-20">[20]</a></sup> With Jakarta selected to host the <a href="/wiki/1962_Asian_Games" title="1962 Asian Games">1962 Asian Games</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soekarno" title="Soekarno">Soekarno</a>, envisaging Jakarta as a great international city, instigated large government-funded projects with openly nationalistic and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modernist_architecture" title="Modernist architecture">modernist architecture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Projects included <a href="/wiki/Semanggi_Interchange" title="Semanggi Interchange">a cloverleaf interchange</a>, a major boulevard (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jalan_MH_Thamrin_(Jakarta)" title="Jalan MH Thamrin (Jakarta)">Jalan MH Thamrin</a>-Sudirman), monuments such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monas" title="Monas">The National Monument</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Indonesia" title="Hotel Indonesia">Hotel Indonesia</a>, a shopping centre, and a new building intended to be the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/CONEFO" title="CONEFO">CONEFO</a>. In October 1965, Jakarta was the site of <a href="/wiki/30_September_Movement" title="30 September Movement">an abortive coup</a> attempt in which six top generals were killed, precipitating <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_mass_killings_of_1965%E2%80%9366" title="Indonesian mass killings of 1965â66">a violent anti-communist purge</a> which killed at least 500,000 people, including some ethnic Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The event marked <a href="/wiki/Transition_to_the_New_Order" title="Transition to the New Order">the beginning of Suharto's New Order</a>. The first government was led by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> until the end of 1960 when the office was changed to that of a <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a>. The last mayor of Jakarta was Soediro until he was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Soemarno_Sosroatmodjo" title="Soemarno Sosroatmodjo">Soemarno Sosroatmodjo</a> as governor. Based on law No. 5 of 1974 relating to regional governments, Jakarta was confirmed as the capital of Indonesia and one of the country's then 26 provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics-2008_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics-2008-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1966, Jakarta was declared a 'special capital region' (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Daerah Khusus Ibukota</i></span>), with a status equivalent to that of a province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Lieutenant General <a href="/wiki/Ali_Sadikin" title="Ali Sadikin">Ali Sadikin</a> served as governor from 1966 to 1977; he rehabilitated roads and bridges, encouraged the arts, built hospitals and a large number of schools. He cleared out slum dwellers for new development projects â some for the benefit of the Suharto family,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>â and attempted to eliminate rickshaws and ban street vendors. He began control of migration to the city to stem overcrowding and poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner1997315_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner1997315-31">[31]</a></sup> Foreign investment contributed to a real estate boom that transformed the face of Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESajor2003713â42_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESajor2003713â42-32">[32]</a></sup> The boom ended with the <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis" title="1997 Asian financial crisis">1997 Asian financial crisis</a>, putting Jakarta at the centre of violence, protest, and political manoeuvring.
</p><p>After three decades in power, support for President <a href="/wiki/Suharto" title="Suharto">Suharto</a> began to wane. Tensions peaked when four students were <a href="/wiki/Trisakti_shootings" title="Trisakti shootings">shot dead</a> at <a href="/wiki/Trisakti_University" title="Trisakti University">Trisakti University</a> by security forces. <a href="/wiki/May_1998_riots_of_Indonesia" title="May 1998 riots of Indonesia">Four days of riots and violence</a> in 1998 ensued that killed an estimated 1,200, and destroyed or damaged 6,000 buildings, forcing Suharto to resign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriend2003329_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriend2003329-33">[33]</a></sup> Much of the rioting targeted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesian" title="Chinese Indonesian">Chinese Indonesians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In the post-Suharto era, Jakarta has remained the focal point of democratic change in Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriend2003?_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriend2003?-35">[35]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jemaah_Islamiah" title="Jemaah Islamiah">Jemaah Islamiah</a>-connected bombings occurred almost annually in the city between 2000 and 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitton2003138â39_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitton2003138â39-20">[20]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/2009_Jakarta_bombings" title="2009 Jakarta bombings">another in 2009</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In August 2007, Jakarta held <a href="/wiki/2007_Jakarta_gubernatorial_election" title="2007 Jakarta gubernatorial election">its first-ever election to choose a governor</a> as part of a nationwide decentralisation program that allows direct local elections in several areas. Previously, governors were elected by the city's legislative body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the Jokowi presidency, the Government adopted a plan to move Indonesia's capital to <a href="/wiki/East_Kalimantan" title="East Kalimantan">East Kalimantan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kalimantan_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-kalimantan-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geography_of_Jakarta" title="Geography of Jakarta">Geography of Jakarta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Floods_in_Jakarta" title="Floods in Jakarta">Floods in Jakarta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Flood_Canal" title="Jakarta Flood Canal">Jakarta Flood Canal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Giant_Sea_Wall_Jakarta" title="Giant Sea Wall Jakarta">Giant Sea Wall Jakarta</a></div>
<p>Jakarta covers 699.5Â km<sup>2</sup> (270.1Â sqÂ mi), the smallest among any <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">Indonesian provinces</a>. However, its metropolitan area covers 6,392Â km<sup>2</sup> (2,468Â sqÂ mi), which extends into two of the bordering provinces of <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banten" title="Banten">Banten</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jabodetabek" title="Jabodetabek">Greater Jakarta</a> area includes three bordering regencies (<a href="/wiki/Bekasi_Regency" title="Bekasi Regency">Bekasi Regency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tangerang_Regency" title="Tangerang Regency">Tangerang Regency</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bogor_Regency" title="Bogor Regency">Bogor Regency</a>) and five adjacent cities (<a href="/wiki/Bogor" title="Bogor">Bogor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Depok" title="Depok">Depok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bekasi" title="Bekasi">Bekasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tangerang" title="Tangerang">Tangerang</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Tangerang" title="South Tangerang">South Tangerang</a>).
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_of_Jakarta_from_Monas.jpg" title="Central Jakarta View from Monas"><img alt="" data-file-height="1934" data-file-width="20357" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/View_of_Jakarta_from_Monas.jpg/1800px-View_of_Jakarta_from_Monas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/View_of_Jakarta_from_Monas.jpg/2700px-View_of_Jakarta_from_Monas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/View_of_Jakarta_from_Monas.jpg/3600px-View_of_Jakarta_from_Monas.jpg 2x" width="1800"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Jakarta_from_Monas.jpg" title="File:View of Jakarta from Monas.jpg"> </a></div>Central Jakarta View from Monas</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_north_jakarta.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Aerial_view_of_north_jakarta.jpg/220px-Aerial_view_of_north_jakarta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Aerial_view_of_north_jakarta.jpg/330px-Aerial_view_of_north_jakarta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Aerial_view_of_north_jakarta.jpg/440px-Aerial_view_of_north_jakarta.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_north_jakarta.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of North Jakarta</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Festival_beach_Ancol_Jakarta.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Festival_beach_Ancol_Jakarta.jpg/220px-Festival_beach_Ancol_Jakarta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Festival_beach_Ancol_Jakarta.jpg/330px-Festival_beach_Ancol_Jakarta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Festival_beach_Ancol_Jakarta.jpg/440px-Festival_beach_Ancol_Jakarta.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Festival_beach_Ancol_Jakarta.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ancol" title="Ancol">Ancol</a> beach</div></div></div>
<p>Jakarta is situated on the northwest coast of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, at the mouth of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciliwung_River" title="Ciliwung River">Ciliwung River</a> on <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Bay" title="Jakarta Bay">Jakarta Bay</a>, an inlet of the <a href="/wiki/Java_Sea" title="Java Sea">Java Sea</a>.  It is strategically located near the <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Strait" title="Sunda Strait">Sunda Strait</a>. The northern part of Jakarta is plain land, some areas of which are below sea level,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> and subject to frequent flooding. The southern parts of the city are hilly. It is one of only two Asian capital cities located in the southern hemisphere (along with <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Dili" title="Dili">Dili</a>). Officially, the area of the Jakarta Special District is 662Â km<sup>2</sup> (256Â sqÂ mi) of land area and 6,977Â km<sup>2</sup> (2,694Â sqÂ mi) of sea area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Islands_(Indonesia)" title="Thousand Islands (Indonesia)">Thousand Islands</a>, which are administratively a part of Jakarta, are located in Jakarta Bay, north of the city.
</p><p>Jakarta lies in a low and flat <a href="/wiki/Alluvial_plain" title="Alluvial plain">alluvial plain</a>, ranging from â2 to 91Â m (â7 to 299Â ft) with an average elevation of 8Â m (26Â ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> with historically extensive swampy areas. Some parts of the city have been constructed on reclaimed tidal flats that occur in around the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurrayClemensPhinnPossingham2014267â72_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayClemensPhinnPossingham2014267â72-42">[42]</a></sup> Thirteen rivers flow through Jakarta. They are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciliwung_River" title="Ciliwung River">Ciliwung River</a>, Kalibaru, <a href="/wiki/Pesanggrahan_River" title="Pesanggrahan River">Pesanggrahan</a>, Cipinang, <a href="/wiki/Angke_River" title="Angke River">Angke River</a>, Maja, Mookervart, Krukut, Buaran, West Tarum, Cakung, Petukangan, <a href="/wiki/Sunter_River" title="Sunter River">Sunter River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grogol_River" title="Grogol River">Grogol River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> They flow from the <a href="/wiki/Puncak" title="Puncak">Puncak</a> highlands to the south of the city, then across the city northwards towards the Java Sea. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciliwung_River" title="Ciliwung River">Ciliwung River</a> divides the city into the western and eastern districts.
</p><p>These rivers, combined with the wet season rains and insufficient drainage due to clogging, make Jakarta prone to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flooding_in_Jakarta" title="Flooding in Jakarta">flooding</a>.
</p><p>Moreover, Jakarta is sinking about 5 to 10Â cm (2.0 to 3.9Â in) each year, and up to 20Â cm (7.9Â in) in the northern coastal areas. After a feasibility study, a ring <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">dyke</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Giant_Sea_Wall_Jakarta" title="Giant Sea Wall Jakarta">Giant Sea Wall Jakarta</a> is under construction around Jakarta Bay to help cope with the threat from the sea. The dyke will be equipped with a pumping system and retention areas to defend against seawater and function as a toll road. The project is expected to be completed by 2025.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> In January 2014, the central government agreed to build two dams in Ciawi, Bogor and a 1.2Â km (0.75Â mi) tunnel from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciliwung_River" title="Ciliwung River">Ciliwung River</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cisadane_River" title="Cisadane River">Cisadane River</a> to ease flooding in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Nowadays, a 1.2Â km (0.75Â mi), with capacity 60Â m<sup>3</sup> (2,100Â cuÂ ft) per second, underground water tunnel between Ciliwung River and the East Flood Canal is being worked on to ease the Ciliwung River overflows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>Environmental advocates point out that subsidence is driven by the extraction of groundwater, much of it illegal. This could be halted by stopping extraction (as the city of Tokyo has done), increasing efficiency, and finding other sources for water use. The rivers of Jakarta are highly polluted and currently unsuitable for drinking water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Colonial_architecture_in_Jakarta" title="Colonial architecture in Jakarta">Colonial architecture in Jakarta</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Jakarta" title="List of tallest buildings in Jakarta">List of tallest buildings in Jakarta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Triangle_of_Jakarta" title="Golden Triangle of Jakarta">Golden Triangle of Jakarta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Javasche_Bank-2010.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Javasche_Bank-2010.JPG/220px-Javasche_Bank-2010.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Javasche_Bank-2010.JPG/330px-Javasche_Bank-2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Javasche_Bank-2010.JPG/440px-Javasche_Bank-2010.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Javasche_Bank-2010.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Facade of the <a href="/wiki/Museum_Bank_Indonesia" title="Museum Bank Indonesia">Museum Bank Indonesia</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kota_Tua" title="Kota Tua">Kota Tua</a></div></div></div>
<p>Jakarta has architecturally significant buildings spanning distinct historical and cultural periods. Architectural styles reflect Malay, Javanese, Arabic, Chinese and Dutch influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKnÃ¶rr2014?_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKnÃ¶rr2014?-49">[49]</a></sup> External influences inform the architecture of the Betawi house. The houses were built of nangka wood (<i><a href="/wiki/Jackfruit" title="Jackfruit">Artocarpus integrifolia</a></i>) and comprise three rooms. The shape of the roof is reminiscent of the traditional <a href="/wiki/Joglo" title="Joglo">Javanese joglo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENasGrijns2000324_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENasGrijns2000324-50">[50]</a></sup> Additionally, the number of registered cultural heritage buildings has increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>Colonial buildings and structures include those that were constructed during the colonial period. The dominant colonial styles can be divided into three periods: the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a> (17th to late 18th century), the transitional style period (late 18th century â 19th century), and Dutch modernism (20th century). Colonial architecture is apparent in houses and villas, churches, civic buildings and offices, mostly concentrated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jakarta_Old_Town" title="Jakarta Old Town">Jakarta Old Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Jakarta" title="Central Jakarta">Central Jakarta</a>. Architects such as J.C. Schultze and <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Cuypers" title="Eduard Cuypers">Eduard Cuypers</a> designed some of the significant buildings. Schultze's works include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gedung_Kesenian_Jakarta" title="Gedung Kesenian Jakarta">Jakarta Art Building</a>, the Indonesia Supreme Court Building and <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_(Indonesia)" title="Ministry of Finance (Indonesia)">Ministry of Finance</a> Building, while Cuypers designed <a href="/wiki/Museum_Bank_Indonesia" title="Museum Bank Indonesia">Bank Indonesia Museum</a> and Bank Mandiri Museum.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BNI_Building.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/BNI_Building.JPG/170px-BNI_Building.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/BNI_Building.JPG/255px-BNI_Building.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/BNI_Building.JPG/340px-BNI_Building.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BNI_Building.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wisma_46" title="Wisma 46">Wisma 46</a> in post-modernist architecture, the fourth tallest building in Jakarta</div></div></div>
<p>In the early 20th century, most buildings were built in <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Neo-Renaissance</a> style. By the 1920s, the architectural taste had begun to shift in favour of <a href="/wiki/Rationalism_(architecture)" title="Rationalism (architecture)">rationalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernism</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">art deco</a> architecture. The elite suburb <a href="/wiki/Menteng" title="Menteng">Menteng</a>, developed during the 1910s, was the city's first attempt at creating ideal and healthy housing for the middle class. The original houses had a longitudinal organisation, with overhanging eaves, large windows and open ventilation, all practical features for a tropical climate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> These houses were developed by N.V. de Bouwploeg, and established by <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Adriaan_Jacobus_Moojen" title="Pieter Adriaan Jacobus Moojen">P.A.J. Moojen</a>.
</p><p>After independence, the process of nation-building in Indonesia and demolishing the memory of colonialism was as important as the symbolic building of arterial roads, monuments, and government buildings. The <a href="/wiki/National_Monument_(Indonesia)" title="National Monument (Indonesia)">National Monument</a> in Jakarta, designed by Sukarno, is Indonesia's beacon of nationalism. In the early 1960s, Jakarta provided highways and super-scale cultural monuments as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senayan_Sports_Stadium" title="Senayan Sports Stadium">Senayan Sports Stadium</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DPR/MPR_Building" title="DPR/MPR Building">parliament building</a> features a hyperbolic roof reminiscent of German rationalist and Corbusian design concepts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBishopPhillipsYeo2003198_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBishopPhillipsYeo2003198-53">[53]</a></sup> Built-in 1996, <a href="/wiki/Wisma_46" title="Wisma 46">Wisma 46</a> soars to a height of 262Â m (860Â ft) and its nib-shaped top celebrates technology and symbolises stereoscopy.
</p><p>The urban construction booms continued during the 21st century. The <a href="/wiki/Golden_Triangle_of_Jakarta" title="Golden Triangle of Jakarta">Golden Triangle of Jakarta</a> is one of the fastest evolving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Business_District" title="Central Business District">CBD</a>'s in the Asia-Pacific region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Council_on_Tall_Buildings_and_Urban_Habitat" title="Council on Tall Buildings and Urban Habitat">CTBUH</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emporis" title="Emporis">Emporis</a>, there are 88 skyscrapers that reach or exceed 150Â m (490Â ft), which puts the city in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_with_the_most_skyscrapers" title="List of cities with the most skyscrapers">top 10 of world rankings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> It has more buildings taller than 150Â metres than any other Southeast Asian or <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> cities.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Indonesia_National-Monument-02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5635" data-file-width="3695" decoding="async" height="336" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Jakarta_Indonesia_National-Monument-02.jpg/220px-Jakarta_Indonesia_National-Monument-02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Jakarta_Indonesia_National-Monument-02.jpg/330px-Jakarta_Indonesia_National-Monument-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Jakarta_Indonesia_National-Monument-02.jpg/440px-Jakarta_Indonesia_National-Monument-02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Indonesia_National-Monument-02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>view of <a href="/wiki/National_Monument_(Indonesia)" title="National Monument (Indonesia)">Monas</a>, Jakarta's landmark</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Bundaran_HI_.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="1632" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Jakarta_Bundaran_HI_.jpg/220px-Jakarta_Bundaran_HI_.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Jakarta_Bundaran_HI_.jpg/330px-Jakarta_Bundaran_HI_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Jakarta_Bundaran_HI_.jpg/440px-Jakarta_Bundaran_HI_.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Bundaran_HI_.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Selamat_Datang_Monument" title="Selamat Datang Monument">Bundaran HI</a>, a 1960s landmark of Jakarta located at the west end of <a href="/wiki/Menteng" title="Menteng">Menteng</a> District.</div></div></div>
<p>Most landmarks, monuments and statues in Jakarta were begun in the 1960s during the <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a> era, then completed in the <a href="/wiki/Suharto" title="Suharto">Suharto</a> era, while some date from the colonial period. Although many of the projects were completed after his presidency, Sukarno, who was an architect, is credited for planning Jakarta's monuments and landmarks, as he desired the city to be the beacon of a powerful new nation. Among the monumental projects were built, initiated, and planned during his administration are the <a href="/wiki/National_Monument_(Indonesia)" title="National Monument (Indonesia)">National Monument</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istiqlal_Mosque,_Jakarta" title="Istiqlal Mosque, Jakarta">Istiqlal mosque</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DPR/MPR_Building" title="DPR/MPR Building">Legislature Building</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gelora_Bung_Karno" title="Gelora Bung Karno">Gelora Bung Karno</a> stadium. Sukarno also built many nationalistic monuments and statues in the capital city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESilver2007101_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESilver2007101-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>The most famous landmark, which became the symbol of the city, is the 132Â m-tall (433Â ft) obelisk of the <a href="/wiki/National_Monument_(Indonesia)" title="National Monument (Indonesia)">National Monument</a> (<i>Monumen Nasional</i> or <i>Monas</i>) in the centre of <a href="/wiki/Merdeka_Square,_Jakarta" title="Merdeka Square, Jakarta">Merdeka Square</a>. On its southwest corner stands a <a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">Mahabharata</a>-themed <a href="/wiki/Arjuna" title="Arjuna">Arjuna</a> <a href="/wiki/Victory" title="Victory">Wijaya</a> chariot statue and fountain. Further south through <a href="/wiki/Jalan_M.H._Thamrin" title="Jalan M.H. Thamrin">Jalan M.H. Thamrin</a>, one of the main avenues, the <a href="/wiki/Selamat_Datang_Monument" title="Selamat Datang Monument"><i>Selamat Datang</i> monument</a> stands on the fountain in the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Indonesia" title="Hotel Indonesia">Hotel Indonesia</a> <a href="/wiki/Roundabout" title="Roundabout">roundabout</a>. Other landmarks include the <a href="/wiki/Istiqlal_Mosque,_Jakarta" title="Istiqlal Mosque, Jakarta">Istiqlal Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Cathedral" title="Jakarta Cathedral">Jakarta Cathedral</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Church,_Jakarta" title="Immanuel Church, Jakarta">Immanuel Church</a>. The former <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_History_Museum" title="Jakarta History Museum">Batavia Stadhuis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kelapa" title="Sunda Kelapa">Sunda Kelapa</a> port in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jakarta_Old_Town" title="Jakarta Old Town">Jakarta Old Town</a> is another landmark. The <a href="/wiki/Gama_Tower" title="Gama Tower">Gama Tower</a> building in <a href="/wiki/South_Jakarta" title="South Jakarta">South Jakarta</a>, at 310Â metres, is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Indonesia" title="List of tallest buildings in Indonesia">tallest building in Indonesia</a>. The most recent landmark built is the <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_International_Stadium" title="Jakarta International Stadium">Jakarta International Stadium</a>.
</p><p>Some of statues and monuments are nationalist, such as the <a href="/wiki/West_Irian_Liberation_Monument" title="West Irian Liberation Monument">West Irian Liberation Monument</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Heroes_Monument,_Jakarta" title="Heroes Monument, Jakarta">Tugu Tani</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Patung_Pemuda_Membangun" title="Patung Pemuda Membangun">Youth statue</a> and the <a class="extiw" href="https://id.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patung_Dirgantara" title="id:Patung Dirgantara">Dirgantara statue</a>. Some statues commemorate <a href="/wiki/National_Hero_of_Indonesia" title="National Hero of Indonesia">Indonesian national heroes</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Diponegoro" title="Diponegoro">Diponegoro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kartini" title="Kartini">Kartini</a> statues in Merdeka Square. The <a href="/wiki/Sudirman" title="Sudirman">Sudirman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Husni_Thamrin" title="Mohammad Husni Thamrin">Thamrin</a> statues are located on the streets bearing their names. There is also a statue of <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Hatta" title="Mohammad Hatta">Hatta</a> at the Proclamation Monument at the entrance to SoekarnoâHatta International Airport.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_lakes">Parks and lakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Parks and lakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boat_ride_at_TMII.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1342" data-file-width="2268" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Boat_ride_at_TMII.jpg/220px-Boat_ride_at_TMII.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Boat_ride_at_TMII.jpg/330px-Boat_ride_at_TMII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Boat_ride_at_TMII.jpg/440px-Boat_ride_at_TMII.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boat_ride_at_TMII.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boat ride at Indonesian archipelago lake in <a href="/wiki/Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah" title="Taman Mini Indonesia Indah">Taman Mini Indonesia Indah</a></div></div></div>
<p>In June 2011, Jakarta had only 10.5% green open spaces (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Ruang Terbuka Hijau</i></span>), although this grew to 13.94%. Public parks are included in public green open spaces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> There are about 300 integrated child-friendly public spaces (RPTRA) in the city in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> As of 2014, 183 water reservoirs and lakes supported the greater Jakarta area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Merdeka_Square,_Jakarta" title="Merdeka Square, Jakarta">Merdeka Square</a> (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Medan Merdeka</i></span>) is an almost 1Â km<sup>2</sup> field housing the symbol of Jakarta, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monas" title="Monas">Monas</a> or <span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Monumen Nasional</i></span> (National Monument). Until 2000, it was the world's largest city square. The square was created by Dutch Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Herman_Willem_Daendels" title="Herman Willem Daendels">Herman Willem Daendels</a> (1810) and was originally named <span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Koningsplein</i></span> (King's Square). On 10 January 1993, President Soeharto started the beautification of the square. Features including a deer park and 33 trees that represent the 33 provinces of Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lapangan_Banteng" title="Lapangan Banteng">Lapangan Banteng</a> (Buffalo Field) is located in Central Jakarta near <a href="/wiki/Istiqlal_Mosque,_Jakarta" title="Istiqlal Mosque, Jakarta">Istiqlal Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Cathedral" title="Jakarta Cathedral">Jakarta Cathedral</a>, and Jakarta Central Post Office. It covers about 4.5 hectares. Initially, it was called <span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Waterlooplein</i></span> and functioned as a ceremonial square during the colonial period. Colonial monuments and memorials erected on the square during the colonial period were demolished during the Sukarno era. The most notable monument in the square is the <span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Monumen Pembebasan Irian Barat</i></span> (Monument of the Liberation of West Irian). During the 1970s and 1980s, the park was used as a bus terminal. In 1993, the park was again turned into a public space. It became a recreation place for people and now serves as an exhibition place or for other events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> 'Jakarta Flona' (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Flora dan Fauna</i></span>), a flower and decoration plants and pet exhibition, is held in this park around August annually.</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cable_car_Gondola_Ancol_Jakarta_Bay_City.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2136" data-file-width="2848" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Cable_car_Gondola_Ancol_Jakarta_Bay_City.jpg/220px-Cable_car_Gondola_Ancol_Jakarta_Bay_City.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Cable_car_Gondola_Ancol_Jakarta_Bay_City.jpg/330px-Cable_car_Gondola_Ancol_Jakarta_Bay_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Cable_car_Gondola_Ancol_Jakarta_Bay_City.jpg/440px-Cable_car_Gondola_Ancol_Jakarta_Bay_City.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cable_car_Gondola_Ancol_Jakarta_Bay_City.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ancol" title="Ancol">Ancol</a> Gondola</div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah" title="Taman Mini Indonesia Indah">Taman Mini Indonesia Indah</a> (Miniature Park of Indonesia), in <a href="/wiki/East_Jakarta" title="East Jakarta">East Jakarta</a>, has ten mini-parks.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taman_Suropati" title="Taman Suropati">Suropati Park</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Menteng" title="Menteng">Menteng</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Jakarta" title="Central Jakarta">Central Jakarta</a>. The park is surrounded by Dutch colonial buildings. Taman Suropati was known as <span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Burgemeester Bisschopplein</i></span> during the colonial time. The park is circular-shaped with a surface area of 16,322Â m<sup>2</sup> (175,690Â sqÂ ft). Several modern statues were made for the park by artists of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">ASEAN</a> countries, which contributes to its nickname '<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Taman persahabatan seniman ASEAN</i></span>' ('Park of the ASEAN artists friendship').<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Menteng_Park" title="Menteng Park">Menteng Park</a> was built on the site of the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persija" title="Persija">Persija</a> football <a href="/wiki/Menteng_Stadium" title="Menteng Stadium">stadium</a>. <a href="/wiki/Situ_Lembang_Park" title="Situ Lembang Park">Situ Lembang Park</a> is also located nearby, which has a lake at the centre.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kalijodo_Park" title="Kalijodo Park">Kalijodo Park</a> is the newest park, in <a href="/wiki/Penjaringan" title="Penjaringan">Penjaringan</a> subdistrict, with 3.4Â ha (8.4 acres) beside the Krendang River. It formally opened on 22 February 2017. The park is open 24 hours as green open space (<i>RTH</i>) and child-friendly integrated public space (<i>RPTRA</i>) and has international-standard skateboard facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muara_Angke_mangrove_forest_and_wildlife_sanctuary" title="Muara Angke mangrove forest and wildlife sanctuary">Muara Angke Wildlife Sanctuary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pantai_Indah_Kapuk" title="Pantai Indah Kapuk">Angke Kapuk Nature Tourism Park</a> at <a href="/wiki/Penjaringan" title="Penjaringan">Penjaringan</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Jakarta" title="North Jakarta">North Jakarta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ragunan_Zoo" title="Ragunan Zoo">Ragunan Zoo</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Pasar_Minggu" title="Pasar Minggu">Pasar Minggu</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Jakarta" title="South Jakarta">South Jakarta</a>. It is the world's third-oldest zoo and is the second-largest with the most diverse animal and plant populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Setu_Babakan" title="Setu Babakan">Setu Babakan</a> is a 32-hectare lake surrounded by Betawi cultural village, located at <a href="/wiki/Jagakarsa" title="Jagakarsa">Jagakarsa</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Jakarta" title="South Jakarta">South Jakarta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Dadap Merah Park is also found in this area.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ancol_Dreamland" title="Ancol Dreamland">Ancol Dreamland</a> is the largest integrated tourism area in Southeast Asia. It is located along the bay, at <a href="/wiki/Ancol" title="Ancol">Ancol</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Jakarta" title="North Jakarta">North Jakarta</a>.</li>
<li>Taman Waduk Pluit/Pluit Lake park and Putra Putri Park at <a href="/wiki/Pluit" title="Pluit">Pluit</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Jakarta" title="North Jakarta">North Jakarta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tebet_Honda_Park" title="Tebet Honda Park">Tebet Honda Park</a>, Puring Park, Mataram Park, Langsat Park, Ayodya Park and Swadharma Park in <a href="/wiki/South_Jakarta" title="South Jakarta">South Jakarta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Jakarta has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon climate</a> (<i>Am</i>) according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="KÃ¶ppen climate classification">KÃ¶ppen climate classification</a> system. The wet season in Jakarta covers seven months: November to May. The remaining five months (June to October) constitute the city's drier season (save for June having an average monthly rainfall of less than 100Â mm (3.9Â in). August qualifies as the genuine dry season month, as it has less than 60Â mm (2.4Â in) of rainfall. As across the western part of Java the wet season rainfall peaks in January and February with average monthly rainfall of 297.7Â mm (11.72Â in), and its dry season's low point is in August with a monthly average of 43.2Â mm (1.70Â in).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-top-width:0;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><caption style="border-top:1px #aaa solid;border-left:1px #aaa style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+200.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1959</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,814,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">8,389,759</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+2.6%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">2010</th><td style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2021</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">10,609,681</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+0.5%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left"><span class="nowrap">Note: Census figures (1950 and 1980) cover</span> the actual and projected populations of the largest asian urban agglomerations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGinsburgKoppelMcGee199171_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGinsburgKoppelMcGee199171-74">[74]</a></sup> According to the Indonesia Central Bureau of Statistics, 23 per cent of urban residents live in poverty. With a population of 7.9Â million in 1985, Jakarta accounted for 19 per cent of the total Indonesia urban population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarphamTanner199571_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarphamTanner199571-75">[75]</a></sup><br/>Source: <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p> Jakarta attracts people from across Indonesia, often in search of employment. The 1961 census showed that 51% of the city's population was born in Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECybriwskyFord2001202â13_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECybriwskyFord2001202â13-78">[78]</a></sup> Inward immigration tended to negate the effect of family planning programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics-2008_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics-2008-28">[28]</a></sup>  Ministry of Home Affairs (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Kemendagri</i></span>) tabulates its own data, which has improved since id card requirements in last decade, lists Jakarta's population at 11,261,595 in yearend 2021.
</p><p>Between 1961 and 1980, the population of Jakarta doubled, and during the period 1980â1990, the city's population grew annually by 3.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The 2010 census counted some 9.58Â million people, well above government estimates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The population rose from 4.5Â million in 1970 to 9.5Â million in 2010, counting only legal residents, while the population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jabodetabek" title="Jabodetabek">Greater Jakarta</a> rose from 8.2Â million in 1970 to 28.5Â million in 2010. As of 2014, the population of Jakarta stood at 10Â million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> with a population density of 15,174 people/km<sup>2</sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHermanto1998?_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHermanto1998?-83">[83]</a></sup> In 2014, the population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jabodetabek" title="Jabodetabek">Greater Jakarta</a> was 30Â million, accounting for 11% of Indonesia's overall population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> It is predicted to reach 35.6Â million people by 2030 to become the world's biggest <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The gender ratio was 102.8 (males per 100 females) in 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and 101.3 in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
