<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Ethnic Groups in Jakarta<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESuryadinataArifinAnanta2003?_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESuryadinataArifinAnanta2003?-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Violet; color:black;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> (36.17%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Brown; color:white;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Betawi_people" title="Betawi people">Betawi</a> (28.29%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Lime; color:black;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> (14.61%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Red; color:black;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesians" title="Chinese Indonesians">Chinese</a> (6.62%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:DarkBlue; color:white;">Â </span>Â <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batak_people" title="Batak people">Batak</a> (3.42%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Gold; color:black;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minang</a> (2.85%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Green; color:white;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Malay_Indonesians" title="Malay Indonesians">Malay</a> (0.96%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Black; color:white;">Â </span>Â Others (7.06%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>Jakarta is pluralistic and religiously diverse, without a majority ethnic group. As of 2010, 36.17% of the city's population were <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a>, 28.29% <a href="/wiki/Betawi_people" title="Betawi people">Betawi</a> (locally established mixed race, cemented by diverse creole), 14.61% <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a>, 6.62% <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesians" title="Chinese Indonesians">Chinese</a>, 3.42% <a href="/wiki/Batak" title="Batak">Batak</a>, 2.85% <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a>, 0.96% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_Malays" title="Ethnic Malays">Malays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indo_people" title="Indo people">Indo</a> and others 7.08%.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jin_De_Yuan,_Chinese_Indonesian.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1630" data-file-width="2268" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Jin_De_Yuan%2C_Chinese_Indonesian.jpg/220px-Jin_De_Yuan%2C_Chinese_Indonesian.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Jin_De_Yuan%2C_Chinese_Indonesian.jpg/330px-Jin_De_Yuan%2C_Chinese_Indonesian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Jin_De_Yuan%2C_Chinese_Indonesian.jpg/440px-Jin_De_Yuan%2C_Chinese_Indonesian.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jin_De_Yuan,_Chinese_Indonesian.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chinese in Jakarta praying during <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a> in Glodok, Jakarta</div></div></div>
<p>The '<a href="/wiki/Betawi_people" title="Betawi people">Betawi</a>' (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Orang Betawi</i></span>, or 'people of Batavia') are immigrant-descendants of the old city who became widely recognised as an ethnic group by the mid-19th century. They mostly descend from an eclectic mix of Southeast Asians brought or attracted to meet labour needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> They are thus a creole ethnic group who came from much of Indonesia. Over generations, most have intermarried with one or more ethnicities, especially people of Chinese, Arab and European descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESÃ¡enzEmbrickRodriguez2015?_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESÃ¡enzEmbrickRodriguez2015?-90">[90]</a></sup> Most Betawis lived in the fringe zones with few Betawi-majority zones of central Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIyer200123_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIyer200123-91">[91]</a></sup> It is thus a conundrum for some Javanese people, especially multi-generational Jakarta residents, to identify as either Javanese or Betawi, since living in a Betawi-majority district and speaking more of that creole and adapting is a matter of preference for such families.
</p><p>A significant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesian" title="Chinese Indonesian">Chinese</a> community has lived in Jakarta for many centuries. They traditionally reside around old urban areas, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinangsia" title="Pinangsia">Pinangsia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pluit" title="Pluit">Pluit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glodok" title="Glodok">Glodok</a> (Jakarta's Chinatown) areas. They also can be found in the old <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinatowns</a> of <a href="/wiki/Senen" title="Senen">Senen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jatinegara" title="Jatinegara">Jatinegara</a>. As of 2001 they self-identified as being 5.5%, which was thought of as under-reported;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> this explains the 6.6% figure ten years later.
</p><p>The Sumatran residents are diverse. According to the 2010 census, roughly 346,000 <a href="/wiki/Batak" title="Batak">Batak</a>, 305,000 <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a> and 155,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_Malays" title="Ethnic Malays">Malays</a> lived in the city. The number of Batak people has grown in ranking, from eighth in 1930 to fifth in 2000. <a href="/wiki/Toba_Batak_people" title="Toba Batak people">Toba Batak</a> is the largest subset in Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReid2010170_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReid2010170-93">[93]</a></sup> Working Minangkabau in the 1980s in high proportions were well-embedded merchants, peddlers, artisans, doctors, teachers or journalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENaim1971?_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENaim1971?-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> is the official and dominant language of Jakarta, while many elderly people speak <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> or <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, depending on their upbringing. <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is used for communication, especially in Central and South Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Each of the ethnic groups uses their mother tongue at home, such as <a href="/wiki/Betawi_language" title="Betawi language">Betawi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_language" title="Sundanese language">Sundanese</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Betawi_language" title="Betawi language">Betawi language</a> is distinct from those of the <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> or <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a>, forming itself as a <a href="/wiki/Language_island" title="Language island">language island</a> in the surrounding area. It is mostly based on the East <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Malay" title="Old Malay">Malay</a> dialect and enriched by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loan_word" title="Loan word">loan words</a> from <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_language" title="Sundanese language">Sundanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hokkien_language" title="Hokkien language">Chinese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, the Betawi language transform into Jakarta <a href="/wiki/Slang" title="Slang">slang</a>, which is all Jakartans used till today no matter which ethnic they are come from.
</p><p>The Chinese in Jakarta mainly speak Indonesian and English, due to strict language-ban during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soeharto" title="Soeharto">Soeharto</a>'s <a href="/wiki/New_Order_(Indonesia)" title="New Order (Indonesia)">new order</a> era, the older may be fluent in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hokkien_dialect" title="Hokkien dialect">Hokkien dialect</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandarin_language" title="Mandarin language">Mandarin</a>, meanwhile the youngster are only fluent in Indonesian and English, some are educated in Mandarin. With recent urbanization within chinese around several rural areas from Indonesia, it bringing other Chinese dialects into the Chinese community in Jakarta such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hakka_language" title="Hakka language">Hakka</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teochew_language" title="Teochew language">Teochew</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cantonese_language" title="Cantonese language">Cantonese</a>. The Hokkien which is mainly from Sumatra (<a href="/wiki/Medan" title="Medan">Medan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bagansiapiapi" title="Bagansiapiapi">Bagansiapiapi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batam" title="Batam">Batam</a>) are mostly spoken in Northern Jakarta, such as <a href="/wiki/Pantai_Indah_Kapuk" title="Pantai Indah Kapuk">Pantai Indah Kapuk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pluit" title="Pluit">Pluit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Glodok" title="Glodok">Glodok</a>, meanwhile Hakka and Teochew which is derived from Chinese community from <a href="/wiki/Pontianak" title="Pontianak">Pontianak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singkawang" title="Singkawang">Singkawang</a> are mainly spoken in West Jakarta like <a href="/wiki/Tambora,_Jakarta" title="Tambora, Jakarta">Tambora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grogol_Petamburan" title="Grogol Petamburan">Grogol Petamburan</a>.
</p><p>The Batak in Jakarta mostly speak Indonesian, while the older generation tend to speak their native languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batak_language" title="Batak language">Batak</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karo_language_(Indonesia)" title="Karo language (Indonesia)">Karo</a>, depending on which ancestral town and places from <a href="/wiki/North_Sumatra" title="North Sumatra">North Sumatra</a> they come from. The Minangkabau mainly speak <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_language" title="Minangkabau language">Minangkabau language</a> aside from Indonesian.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div class="mw-no-invert" style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black;transform:scaleX(-1)rotate(-90deg)">

<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkBlue"></div>

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religion in Jakarta (2021)
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:DarkGreen; color:white;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (83.68%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:DarkBlue; color:white;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> (8.6%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Purple; color:white;">Â </span>Â <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a> (3.93%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Gold; color:black;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (3.59%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:DarkOrange; color:black;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (0.18%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:red; color:black;">Â </span>Â <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> (0.02%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>In 2017, Jakarta's religious composition was distributed over <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (83.43%), <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> (8.63%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a> (4.0%), <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (3.74%), <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (0.19%), and <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> (0.01%). About 231 people claimed to follow folk religions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most <span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id"><a href="/wiki/Pesantren" title="Pesantren">pesantren</a></i></span> (Islamic boarding schools) in Jakarta are affiliated with the traditionalist <a href="/wiki/Nahdlatul_Ulama" title="Nahdlatul Ulama">Nahdlatul Ulama</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> modernist organisations mostly catering to a socioeconomic class of educated urban elites and merchant traders. They give priority to education, social welfare programs and religious propagation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPorter200239_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPorter200239-99">[99]</a></sup> Many Islamic organisations have headquarters in Jakarta, including <a href="/wiki/Nahdlatul_Ulama" title="Nahdlatul Ulama">Nahdlatul Ulama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Ulema_Council" title="Indonesian Ulema Council">Indonesian Ulema Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhammadiyah" title="Muhammadiyah">Muhammadiyah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jaringan_Islam_Liberal" title="Jaringan Islam Liberal">Jaringan Islam Liberal</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> community has a <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_(religious_jurisdiction)" title="Metropolis (religious jurisdiction)">Metropolis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Jakarta" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Jakarta">Archdiocese of Jakarta</a> that includes <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a> as part of the ecclesiastical province. Jakarta also host the largest <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> adherent in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Java_Island" title="Java Island">Java Island</a>, where most of the followers are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesian" title="Chinese Indonesian">Chinese</a>, The city also has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> community, which mainly are from <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Indonesians" title="Indian Indonesians">Indian</a> people. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="BahÃ¡Ê¼Ã­ Faith">BahÃ¡Ê¼Ã­ Faith</a> community presence in Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Companies_of_Indonesia" title="Category:Companies of Indonesia">Category:Companies of Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia_Stock_Exchange.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1150" decoding="async" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Indonesia_Stock_Exchange.jpg/170px-Indonesia_Stock_Exchange.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Indonesia_Stock_Exchange.jpg/255px-Indonesia_Stock_Exchange.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Indonesia_Stock_Exchange.jpg/340px-Indonesia_Stock_Exchange.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia_Stock_Exchange.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indonesian_Stock_Exchange" title="Indonesian Stock Exchange">Indonesian Stock Exchange</a> (Bursa Efek Indonesia) building in Jakarta, one of the oldest in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia is the largest economy of <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>, and Jakarta is the economic nerve centre of the Indonesian archipelago. Jakarta's nominal GDP was US$483.8Â billion in 2016, which is about 17.5% of Indonesia's.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Jakarta ranked at 21 in the list of <i>Cities Of Economic Influence Index</i> in 2020 by CEOWORLD magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> According to the <i>Japan Center for Economic Research</i>, <a href="/wiki/Gross_regional_product" title="Gross regional product">GRP</a> per capita of Jakarta will rank 28th among the 77 cities in 2030 from 41st in 2015, the largest in Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Savills" title="Savills">Savills</a> Resilient Cities Index has predicted Jakarta to be within the top 20 cities in the world by 2028.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jakarta's economy depends highly on manufacturing and service sectors such as banking, trading and financial. Industries include electronics, automotive, chemicals, mechanical engineering and biomedical sciences. The head office of <a href="/wiki/Bank_Indonesia" title="Bank Indonesia">Bank Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_Stock_Exchange" title="Indonesia Stock Exchange">Indonesia Stock Exchange</a> are located in the city. Most of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State-owned_Enterprise_of_Indonesia" title="State-owned Enterprise of Indonesia">SOEs</a> include <a href="/wiki/Pertamina" title="Pertamina">Pertamina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perusahaan_Listrik_Negara" title="Perusahaan Listrik Negara">PLN</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angkasa_Pura" title="Angkasa Pura">Angkasa Pura</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telkomsel" title="Telkomsel">Telkomsel</a> operate head offices in the city, as do major <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Indonesia" title="List of companies of Indonesia">Indonesian conglomerates</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Salim_Group" title="Salim Group">Salim Group</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinar_Mas_Group" title="Sinar Mas Group">Sinar Mas Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astra_International" title="Astra International">Astra International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gudang_Garam" title="Gudang Garam">Gudang Garam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kompas_Gramedia_Group" title="Kompas Gramedia Group">Kompas-Gramedia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Media_Nusantara_Citra" title="Media Nusantara Citra">MNC Group</a>. The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Chamber_of_Commerce_and_Industry" title="Indonesian Chamber of Commerce and Industry">Indonesian Chamber of Commerce and Industry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Employers_Association" title="Indonesian Employers Association">Indonesian Employers Association</a> are also located in the city. As of 2017, the city is home to six <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Global_2000" title="Forbes Global 2000">Forbes Global 2000</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> and seven <a href="/wiki/Unicorn_(finance)" title="Unicorn (finance)">Unicorn</a> companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alibaba_group" title="Alibaba group">Alibaba</a> have regional cloud centers in Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arjuna_Wijaya_chariot_statue_in_Jakarta.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1610" data-file-width="2268" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Arjuna_Wijaya_chariot_statue_in_Jakarta.jpg/220px-Arjuna_Wijaya_chariot_statue_in_Jakarta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Arjuna_Wijaya_chariot_statue_in_Jakarta.jpg/330px-Arjuna_Wijaya_chariot_statue_in_Jakarta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Arjuna_Wijaya_chariot_statue_in_Jakarta.jpg/440px-Arjuna_Wijaya_chariot_statue_in_Jakarta.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arjuna_Wijaya_chariot_statue_in_Jakarta.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bank_Indonesia" title="Bank Indonesia">Bank Indonesia</a> head office</div></div></div>
<p>As of 2018, Jakarta contributes about 17% of Indonesia's GRDP (<a href="/wiki/Gross_regional_domestic_product" title="Gross regional domestic product">Gross Regional Domestic Product</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> In 2017, the economic growth was 6.22%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Throughout the same year, the total value of investment was Rp 108.6Â trillion (US$8Â billion), an increase of 84.7% from the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> In 2015, GDP per capita was estimated at Rp 194.87Â million (US$14,570).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The most significant contributions to GRDP were by finance, ownership and business services (29%); trade, hotel and restaurant sector (20%), and manufacturing industry sector (16%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics-2008_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics-2008-28">[28]</a></sup> In 2007, the increase in per capita GRDP of Jakarta inhabitants was 11.6% compared to the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics-2008_28-3"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics-2008-28">[28]</a></sup> Both GRDP by at current market price and GRDP by at 2000 constant price in 2007 for the Municipality of Central Jakarta, which was Rp 146Â million and Rp 81Â million, was higher than other municipalities in Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics-2008_28-4"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics-2008-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Wealth Report 2015 by <a href="/wiki/Knight_Frank" title="Knight Frank">Knight Frank</a> reported that 24 individuals in Indonesia in 2014 had wealth at least US$1Â billion and 18 live in Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The cost of living continues to rise. Both land price and rents have become expensive. <a href="/wiki/Mercer_(consulting_firm)" title="Mercer (consulting firm)">Mercer</a>'s <i>2017 Cost of Living Survey</i> ranked Jakarta as 88th costliest city in the world for expatriates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Industrial development and the construction of new housing thrive on the outskirts, while commerce and banking remain concentrated in the city centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Jakarta has a bustling luxury property market. <a href="/wiki/Knight_Frank" title="Knight Frank">Knight Frank</a>, a global real estate consultancy based in London, reported in 2014 that Jakarta offered the highest return on high-end property investment in the world in 2013, citing a supply shortage and a sharply depreciated currency as reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_skyline_at_night._Business_District_area_at_Jalan_Rasuna_Said,_South_Jakarta,_as_seen_from_Kuningan_District,_South_Jakarta,_Indonesia.jpg" title="Golden Triangle, extending from Central Jakarta to South Jakarta. Most of the city's foreign embassies and tallest skyscrapers are located in the area, which is the main CBD of Jakarta."><img alt="" data-file-height="3063" data-file-width="9938" decoding="async" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Jakarta_skyline_at_night._Business_District_area_at_Jalan_Rasuna_Said%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_as_seen_from_Kuningan_District%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia.jpg/800px-Jakarta_skyline_at_night._Business_District_area_at_Jalan_Rasuna_Said%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_as_seen_from_Kuningan_District%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Jakarta_skyline_at_night._Business_District_area_at_Jalan_Rasuna_Said%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_as_seen_from_Kuningan_District%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia.jpg/1200px-Jakarta_skyline_at_night._Business_District_area_at_Jalan_Rasuna_Said%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_as_seen_from_Kuningan_District%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Jakarta_skyline_at_night._Business_District_area_at_Jalan_Rasuna_Said%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_as_seen_from_Kuningan_District%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia.jpg/1600px-Jakarta_skyline_at_night._Business_District_area_at_Jalan_Rasuna_Said%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_as_seen_from_Kuningan_District%2C_South_Jakarta%2C_Indonesia.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_skyline_at_night._Business_District_area_at_Jalan_Rasuna_Said,_South_Jakarta,_as_seen_from_Kuningan_District,_South_Jakarta,_Indonesia.jpg" title="File:Jakarta skyline at night. Business District area at Jalan Rasuna Said, South Jakarta, as seen from Kuningan District, South Jakarta, Indonesia.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Golden_Triangle_of_Jakarta" title="Golden Triangle of Jakarta">Golden Triangle</a>, extending from <a href="/wiki/Central_Jakarta" title="Central Jakarta">Central Jakarta</a> to <a href="/wiki/South_Jakarta" title="South Jakarta">South Jakarta</a>. Most of the city's foreign embassies and tallest skyscrapers are located in the area, which is the main <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">CBD</a> of Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Jakarta" title="List of shopping malls in Jakarta">List of shopping malls in Jakarta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia-Korea_Culture_Exchange_2010_Ceramic_Show.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Indonesia-Korea_Culture_Exchange_2010_Ceramic_Show.JPG/220px-Indonesia-Korea_Culture_Exchange_2010_Ceramic_Show.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Indonesia-Korea_Culture_Exchange_2010_Ceramic_Show.JPG/330px-Indonesia-Korea_Culture_Exchange_2010_Ceramic_Show.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Indonesia-Korea_Culture_Exchange_2010_Ceramic_Show.JPG/440px-Indonesia-Korea_Culture_Exchange_2010_Ceramic_Show.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia-Korea_Culture_Exchange_2010_Ceramic_Show.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gandaria_City" title="Gandaria City">Gandaria City</a> Mall in <a href="/wiki/South_Jakarta" title="South Jakarta">South Jakarta</a></div></div></div>
<p>As of 2015, with a total of 550 hectares, Jakarta had the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_malls_in_Jakarta" title="List of malls in Jakarta">shopping mall floor area</a> within a single city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Malls include <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Indonesia" title="Plaza Indonesia">Plaza Indonesia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Indonesia" title="Grand Indonesia">Grand Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Senayan" title="Plaza Senayan">Plaza Senayan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senayan_City" title="Senayan City">Senayan City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Place_Jakarta" title="Pacific Place Jakarta">Pacific Place</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gandaria_City" title="Gandaria City">Gandaria City</a>, ÃON Mall Tanjung Barat, <a href="/wiki/Mall_Taman_Anggrek" title="Mall Taman Anggrek">Mall Taman Anggrek</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pondok_Indah_Mall" title="Pondok Indah Mall">Pondok Indah Mall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Fashion retail brands in Jakarta include <a href="/wiki/Debenhams" title="Debenhams">Debenhams</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Senayan_City" title="Senayan City">Senayan City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kemang_Village" title="Kemang Village">Lippo Mall Kemang Village</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Japanese <a href="/wiki/Sogo" title="Sogo">Sogo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Seibu_Department_Stores" title="Seibu Department Stores">Seibu</a> in Grand Indonesia Shopping Town, and French brand, <a href="/wiki/Galeries_Lafayette" title="Galeries Lafayette">Galeries Lafayette</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Place_Jakarta" title="Pacific Place Jakarta">Pacific Place</a>. The new Satrio-Casablanca shopping belt includes centres such as <a href="/wiki/Kuningan_City" title="Kuningan City">Kuningan City</a>, Mal Ambassador, <a href="/wiki/Kota_Kasablanka" title="Kota Kasablanka">Kota Kasablanka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ciputra_World_Jakarta" title="Ciputra World Jakarta">Lotte Shopping Avenue</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Shopping malls are also located at <a href="/wiki/Grogol" title="Grogol">Grogol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puri_Indah" title="Puri Indah">Puri Indah</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Jakarta" title="West Jakarta">West Jakarta</a>.
</p><p>Traditional markets include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blok_M" title="Blok M">Blok M</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayestik_Market" title="Mayestik Market">Pasar Mayestik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanah_Abang" title="Tanah Abang">Tanah Abang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senen" title="Senen">Senen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pasar_Baru" title="Pasar Baru">Pasar Baru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glodok" title="Glodok">Glodok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mangga_Dua,_Jakarta" title="Mangga Dua, Jakarta">Mangga Dua</a>, Cempaka Mas, and <a href="/wiki/Jatinegara" title="Jatinegara">Jatinegara</a>. Special markets sell <a href="/wiki/Antique" title="Antique">antique</a> goods at Surabaya Street and gemstones in Rawabening Market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Indonesia" title="Tourism in Indonesia">Tourism in Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_and_cultural_institutions_in_Indonesia" title="List of museums and cultural institutions in Indonesia">List of museums and cultural institutions in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Indonesia_Post-office-at-Fatahillah-Square-01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2843" data-file-width="5540" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Jakarta_Indonesia_Post-office-at-Fatahillah-Square-01.jpg/250px-Jakarta_Indonesia_Post-office-at-Fatahillah-Square-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Jakarta_Indonesia_Post-office-at-Fatahillah-Square-01.jpg/375px-Jakarta_Indonesia_Post-office-at-Fatahillah-Square-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Jakarta_Indonesia_Post-office-at-Fatahillah-Square-01.jpg/500px-Jakarta_Indonesia_Post-office-at-Fatahillah-Square-01.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Indonesia_Post-office-at-Fatahillah-Square-01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jakarta Old City Post Office at Fatahillah Square, Central Jakarta</div></div></div><p>
Though Jakarta has been named the most popular location as per tag stories,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> and ranked eighth most-posted among the cities in the world in 2017 on image-sharing site <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> it is not a top international tourist destination. The city, however, is ranked as the fifth fastest-growing tourist destination among 132 cities according to <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_international_visitors" title="List of cities by international visitors">MasterCard Global Destination Cities Index</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Travel_and_Tourism_Council" title="World Travel and Tourism Council">World Travel and Tourism Council</a> also listed Jakarta as among the top ten fastest-growing tourism cities in the world in 2017<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> and categorised it as an <i>emerging performer</i>, which will see a significant increase in tourist arrivals in less than ten years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> According to <i>Euromonitor International's latest Top 100 City Destinations Ranking</i> of 2019, Jakarta ranked at 57th among 100 most visited cities of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah_Map_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="783" data-file-width="1170" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah_Map_en.svg/220px-Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah_Map_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah_Map_en.svg/330px-Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah_Map_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah_Map_en.svg/440px-Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah_Map_en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah_Map_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Most visitors to Jakarta are domestic tourists, and <a href="/wiki/Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah" title="Taman Mini Indonesia Indah">Taman Mini Indonesia Indah</a> is aimed at supporting national identity and patriotism.</div></div></div><p>Most of the visitors attracted to Jakarta are domestic tourists. As the gateway of <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, Jakarta often serves as a stop-over for foreign visitors on their way to other Indonesian tourist destinations such as <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lombok" title="Lombok">Lombok</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Komodo_Island" title="Komodo Island">Komodo Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yogyakarta" title="Yogyakarta">Yogyakarta</a>. Jakarta is trying to attract more international tourist by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meetings,_incentives,_conferencing,_exhibitions" title="Meetings, incentives, conferencing, exhibitions">MICE</a> tourism, by arranging increasing numbers of <a href="/wiki/Convention_(meeting)" title="Convention (meeting)">conventions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In 2012, the tourism sector contributed Rp. 2.6Â trillion (US$268.5Â million) to the city's total direct income of Rp. 17.83Â trillion (US$1.45Â billion), a 17.9% increase from the previous year 2011.
</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Indonesia" title="List of universities in Indonesia">List of universities in Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Indonesia" title="List of schools in Indonesia">List of schools in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atma_jaya.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2247" data-file-width="2427" decoding="async" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Atma_jaya.jpg/220px-Atma_jaya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Atma_jaya.jpg/330px-Atma_jaya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Atma_jaya.jpg/440px-Atma_jaya.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atma_jaya.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Atma_Jaya_Catholic_University_of_Indonesia" title="Atma Jaya Catholic University of Indonesia">Atma Jaya Catholic University of Indonesia</a> campus at <a href="/wiki/Semanggi_Interchange" title="Semanggi Interchange">Semanggi</a></div></div></div>
<p>Jakarta is home to numerous educational institutions. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Indonesia" title="University of Indonesia">University of Indonesia</a> (UI) is the largest and oldest tertiary-level educational institution in Indonesia. It is a public institution with campuses in Salemba (Central Jakarta) and in <a href="/wiki/Depok" title="Depok">Depok</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> The three other public universities in Jakarta are <a href="/wiki/Syarif_Hidayatullah_State_Islamic_University_Jakarta" title="Syarif Hidayatullah State Islamic University Jakarta">Syarif Hidayatullah State Islamic University Jakarta</a>, the State University of Jakarta  (UNJ),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> and the University of Pembangunan Nasional 'Veteran' Jakarta (UPN "Veteran" Jakarta).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> There is a vocational higher education, <a class="external text" href="https://pnj.ac.id" rel="nofollow">Politeknik Negeri Jakarta (PNJ)</a>. Some major private universities in Jakarta are <a href="/wiki/Trisakti_University" title="Trisakti University">Trisakti University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Christian_University_of_Indonesia" title="The Christian University of Indonesia">The Christian University of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercu_Buana_University" title="Mercu Buana University">Mercu Buana University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarumanagara_University" title="Tarumanagara University">Tarumanagara University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atma_Jaya_Catholic_University_of_Indonesia" title="Atma Jaya Catholic University of Indonesia">Atma Jaya Catholic University of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pelita_Harapan_University" title="Pelita Harapan University">Pelita Harapan University</a>, Pertamina University,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bina_Nusantara_University" title="Bina Nusantara University">Bina Nusantara University</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Jayabaya University,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> and Pancasila University.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fakultas_Kedokteran_Universitas_Indonesia.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Fakultas_Kedokteran_Universitas_Indonesia.JPG/220px-Fakultas_Kedokteran_Universitas_Indonesia.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Fakultas_Kedokteran_Universitas_Indonesia.JPG/330px-Fakultas_Kedokteran_Universitas_Indonesia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Fakultas_Kedokteran_Universitas_Indonesia.JPG/440px-Fakultas_Kedokteran_Universitas_Indonesia.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fakultas_Kedokteran_Universitas_Indonesia.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/University_of_Indonesia" title="University of Indonesia">University of Indonesia</a> <a href="/wiki/Salemba" title="Salemba">Salemba</a> campus</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/STOVIA" title="STOVIA">STOVIA</a> (<i>School tot Opleiding van Indische Artsen,</i> now <i>Universitas Indonesia</i>) was the first high school in Jakarta, established in 1851.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Jakarta houses many students from around Indonesia, many of whom reside in dormitories or home-stay residences. For basic education, a variety of primary and secondary schools are available, tagged with the public (<i>national</i>), private (<i>national and bi-lingual national plus</i>) and <i>international</i> labels. Four of the major international schools are the <a href="/wiki/Gandhi_Memorial_International_School" title="Gandhi Memorial International School">Gandhi Memorial International School</a>, IPEKA International Christian School,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Intercultural_School" title="Jakarta Intercultural School">Jakarta Intercultural School</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_School_Jakarta" title="British School Jakarta">British School Jakarta</a>. Other international schools include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jakarta_International_Korean_School" title="Jakarta International Korean School">Jakarta International Korean School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bina_Bangsa_School" title="Bina Bangsa School">Bina Bangsa School</a>, Jakarta International Multicultural School,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_International_School,_Indonesia" title="Australian International School, Indonesia">Australian International School</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> New Zealand International School,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Singapore_International_School" title="Singapore International School">Singapore International School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Japanese_School" title="Jakarta Japanese School">Jakarta Japanese School</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sekolah_Pelita_Harapan" title="Sekolah Pelita Harapan">Sekolah Pelita Harapan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_contemporary_life">Culture and contemporary life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture and contemporary life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As the capital of Indonesia, Jakarta is a melting pot of cultures from all ethnic groups of the country. Though <a href="/wiki/Betawi_people" title="Betawi people">Betawi people</a> are an indigenous community of Jakarta, the city's culture represents many languages and ethnic groups, support differences regarding religion, traditions and linguistics, rather than any single and dominant culture.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_festivals">Arts and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Arts and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tanjidor,_by_M_Jeffry_Hanafiah.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2003" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Tanjidor%2C_by_M_Jeffry_Hanafiah.jpg/220px-Tanjidor%2C_by_M_Jeffry_Hanafiah.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Tanjidor%2C_by_M_Jeffry_Hanafiah.jpg/330px-Tanjidor%2C_by_M_Jeffry_Hanafiah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Tanjidor%2C_by_M_Jeffry_Hanafiah.jpg/440px-Tanjidor%2C_by_M_Jeffry_Hanafiah.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tanjidor,_by_M_Jeffry_Hanafiah.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tanjidor" title="Tanjidor">Tanjidor</a> music of <a href="/wiki/Betawi_people" title="Betawi people">Betawi</a> culture demonstrate <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Indonesians" title="Portuguese Indonesians">European</a> influence</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Betawi_people" title="Betawi people">Betawi</a> culture is distinct from those of the <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> or <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a>, forming a <a href="/wiki/Language_island" title="Language island">language island</a> in the surrounding area. Betawi arts have a low profile in Jakarta, and most Betawi people have moved to the suburbs. The cultures of the Javanese and other Indonesian ethnic groups have a higher profile than that of the Betawi. There is a significant Chinese influence in Betawi culture, reflected in the popularity of Chinese cakes and sweets, <a href="/wiki/Firecracker" title="Firecracker">firecrackers</a> and Betawi wedding attire that demonstrates Chinese and Arab influences.
</p><p>Some festivals such as the <i>Jalan Jaksa Festival</i>, <i>Kemang Festival</i>, <i>Festival Condet</i> and <i>Lebaran Betawi</i> include efforts to preserve Betawi arts by inviting artists to display performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> Jakarta has several performing art centres, such as the classical concert hall Aula Simfonia Jakarta in Kemayoran, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taman_Ismail_Marzuki" title="Taman Ismail Marzuki">Taman Ismail Marzuki</a> (TIM) art centre in Cikini, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gedung_Kesenian_Jakarta" title="Gedung Kesenian Jakarta">Gedung Kesenian Jakarta</a> near Pasar Baru, Balai Sarbini in the Plaza Semanggi area, <a href="/wiki/Bentara_Budaya_Jakarta" title="Bentara Budaya Jakarta">Bentara Budaya Jakarta</a> in the Palmerah area, Pasar Seni (Art Market) in <a href="/wiki/Ancol_Dreamland" title="Ancol Dreamland">Ancol</a>, and traditional Indonesian art performances at the pavilions of some provinces in <a href="/wiki/Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah" title="Taman Mini Indonesia Indah">Taman Mini Indonesia Indah</a>. Traditional music is often found at high-class hotels, including <a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">Wayang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">Gamelan</a> performances. Javanese <a href="/wiki/Wayang_wong" title="Wayang wong">Wayang Orang</a> performances can be found at Wayang Orang Bharata theatre.
</p><p>Arts and culture festivals and exhibitions include the annual ARKIPEL â Jakarta International Documentary and Experimental Film Festival, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_International_Film_Festival" title="Jakarta International Film Festival">Jakarta International Film Festival</a> (JiFFest), <a href="/wiki/Djakarta_Warehouse_Project" title="Djakarta Warehouse Project">Djakarta Warehouse Project</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Fashion_Week" title="Jakarta Fashion Week">Jakarta Fashion Week</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Fashion_%26_Food_Festival" title="Jakarta Fashion &amp; Food Festival">Jakarta Fashion &amp; Food Festival</a> (JFFF), <a href="/wiki/Jakarnaval" title="Jakarnaval">Jakarnaval</a>, Jakarta Night Festival, Kota Tua Creative Festival, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_International_Book_Fair" title="Indonesia International Book Fair">Indonesia International Book Fair</a> (IIBF), Indonesia Creative Products and Jakarta Arts and Crafts exhibition. <a href="/wiki/Art_Jakarta" title="Art Jakarta">Art Jakarta</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a> <a href="/wiki/Fair" title="Fair">fair</a>, which is held annually. <i>Flona Jakarta</i> is a flora-and-fauna exhibition, held annually in August at <a href="/wiki/Lapangan_Banteng" title="Lapangan Banteng">Lapangan Banteng</a> Park, featuring flowers, plant nurseries, and pets. <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Fair" title="Jakarta Fair">Jakarta Fair</a> is held annually from mid-June to mid-July to celebrate the anniversary of the city and is mostly centred around a trade fair. However, this month-long fair also features entertainment, including arts and music performances by local musicians. <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_International_Java_Jazz_Festival" title="Jakarta International Java Jazz Festival">Jakarta International Java Jazz Festival</a> (JJF) is one of the largest jazz festivals in the world, the biggest in the Southern hemisphere, and is held annually in March.
</p><p>Several foreign art and culture centres in Jakarta promote culture and language through learning centres, libraries and art galleries. These include the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Confucius_Institute" title="Confucius Institute">Confucius Institute</a>, the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_House_(Jakarta)" title="Erasmus House (Jakarta)">Erasmus Huis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Council" title="British Council">British Council</a>, the French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alliance_Fran%C3%A7aise" title="Alliance FranÃ§aise">Alliance FranÃ§aise</a>, the German <a href="/wiki/Goethe-Institut" title="Goethe-Institut">Goethe-Institut</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Foundation" title="Japan Foundation">Japan Foundation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Council_for_Cultural_Relations" title="Indian Council for Cultural Relations">Jawaharlal Nehru Indian Cultural Center</a>.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
