<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Betawi_cuisine" title="Betawi cuisine">Betawi cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gado-gado_in_Jakarta.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Gado-gado_in_Jakarta.JPG/220px-Gado-gado_in_Jakarta.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Gado-gado_in_Jakarta.JPG/330px-Gado-gado_in_Jakarta.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Gado-gado_in_Jakarta.JPG/440px-Gado-gado_in_Jakarta.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gado-gado_in_Jakarta.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Gado-gado" title="Gado-gado">Gado-gado</a></i> is a popular <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_cuisine" title="Indonesian cuisine">Indonesian</a> <a href="/wiki/Salad" title="Salad">salad</a> dish.</div></div></div>
<p>All varieties of <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_cuisine" title="Indonesian cuisine">Indonesian cuisine</a> have a presence in Jakarta. The local cuisine is <a href="/wiki/Betawi_cuisine" title="Betawi cuisine">Betawi cuisine</a>, which reflects various foreign culinary traditions. Betawi cuisine is heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Peranakan_cuisine" title="Peranakan cuisine">Malay-Chinese Peranakan cuisine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_cuisine" title="Sundanese cuisine">Sundanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_cuisine" title="Javanese cuisine">Javanese cuisine</a>, which is also influenced by Indian, Arabic and European cuisines. One of the most popular local dishes of Betawi cuisine is <i><a href="/wiki/Soto_(food)#Varieties" title="Soto (food)">Soto</a> <a href="/wiki/Betawi_people" title="Betawi people">Betawi</a></i> which is prepared from chunks of beef and <a href="/wiki/Offal" title="Offal">offal</a> in rich and spicy cow's milk or coconut milk broth. Other popular Betawi dishes include <i><a href="/wiki/Soto_(food)" title="Soto (food)">soto kaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nasi_uduk" title="Nasi uduk">nasi uduk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerak_telor" title="Kerak telor">kerak telor</a></i> (spicy omelette), <i><a href="/wiki/Nasi_ulam" title="Nasi ulam">nasi ulam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asinan" title="Asinan">asinan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ketoprak_(dish)" title="Ketoprak (dish)">ketoprak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rojak#Rujak_Juhi" title="Rojak">rujak</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Gado-gado" title="Gado-gado">gado-gado</a></i> Betawi (salad in peanut sauce).
</p><p>Jakarta cuisine can be found in modest street-side <i><a href="/wiki/Warung" title="Warung">warung</a></i> food stalls and <i>kaki lima</i> (five legs) travelling vendors to high-end fine dining restaurants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Live music venues and exclusive restaurants are abundant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> Many traditional foods from far-flung regions in Indonesia can be found in Jakarta. For example, traditional <a href="/wiki/Padang_cuisine#Padang_restaurants" title="Padang cuisine">Padang restaurants</a> and low-budget <i><a href="/wiki/Warung#Varieties" title="Warung">Warteg</a></i> (<i>Warung Tegal</i>) food-stalls are ubiquitous in the capital. Other popular street foods include <i><a href="/wiki/Nasi_goreng" title="Nasi goreng">nasi goreng</a></i> (fried rice), <i><a href="/wiki/Satay" title="Satay">sate</a></i> (skewered meats), <i><a href="/wiki/Pecel_lele" title="Pecel lele">pecel lele</a></i> (fried catfish), <i><a href="/wiki/Bakso" title="Bakso">bakso</a></i> (meatballs), <i><a href="/wiki/Baozi" title="Baozi">bakpau</a></i> (Chinese bun) and <i><a href="/wiki/Siomay" title="Siomay">siomay</a></i> (fish dumplings).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jalan_Jaksa" title="Jalan Jaksa">Jalan Sabang</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Jalan Sidoarjo, Jalan Kendal at <a href="/wiki/Kebon_Sirih,_Menteng" title="Kebon Sirih, Menteng">Menteng</a> area, <a href="/wiki/Kota_Tua_Jakarta" title="Kota Tua Jakarta">Kota Tua</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kebayoran_Baru,_South_Jakarta" title="Kebayoran Baru, South Jakarta">Blok S</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blok_M" title="Blok M">Blok M</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tebet,_South_Jakarta" title="Tebet, South Jakarta">Jalan Tebet</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> are all popular destinations for street-food lovers.
Trendy restaurants, cafe and bars can be found at <a href="/wiki/Menteng" title="Menteng">Menteng</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kemang,_Jakarta" title="Kemang, Jakarta">Kemang</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SCBD" title="SCBD">Jalan Senopati</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Setiabudi,_South_Jakarta" title="Setiabudi, South Jakarta">Kuningan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senayan_City" title="Senayan City">Senayan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pantai_Indah_Kapuk" title="Pantai Indah Kapuk">Pantai Indah Kapuk</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kelapa_Gading" title="Kelapa Gading">Kelapa Gading</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">Chinese</a> street-food is plentiful at Jalan Pangeran, <a href="/wiki/Mangga_Besar,_Jakarta" title="Mangga Besar, Jakarta">Manga Besar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glodok" title="Glodok">Petak Sembilan</a> in the old Jakarta area, while the <i>Little Tokyo</i> area of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blok_M" title="Blok M">Blok M</a> has many <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cuisine" title="Japanese cuisine">Japanese</a> style restaurants and bars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lenggang_Jakarta" title="Lenggang Jakarta">Lenggang Jakarta</a> is a food court, accommodating small traders and street vendors,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indonesian_Cuisine" title="Indonesian Cuisine">Indonesian foods</a> are available within a single compound. At present, there are two such food courts, located at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monas" title="Monas">Monas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kemayoran" title="Kemayoran">Kemayoran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thamrin_10" title="Thamrin 10">Thamrin 10</a> is a food and creative park located at Menteng, where varieties of food stall are available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>
</p><p>Global fast-food chains are present, and usually found in <a href="/wiki/List_of_shopping_malls_in_Jakarta" title="List of shopping malls in Jakarta">Shopping malls</a>, along with local brands like <a href="/wiki/J.CO_Donuts" title="J.CO Donuts">J'CO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Es_Teler_77" title="Es Teler 77">Es Teler 77</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kebab_Turki_Baba_Rafi" title="Kebab Turki Baba Rafi">Kebab Turki</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_Fried_Chicken" title="California Fried Chicken">CFC</a>, and Japanese <a href="/wiki/HokBen" title="HokBen">HokBen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yoshinoya" title="Yoshinoya">Yoshinoya</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Foreign cuisines such as <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cuisine" title="Japanese cuisine">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_cuisine" title="Korean cuisine">Korean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_cuisine" title="Thai cuisine">Thai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_cuisine" title="Singaporean cuisine">Singaporean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_cuisine" title="Indian cuisine">Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_cuisine" title="American cuisine">American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australian_cuisine" title="Australian cuisine">Australian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malaysian_Cuisine" title="Malaysian Cuisine">Malaysian</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_cuisine" title="French cuisine">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_cuisine" title="Mediterranean cuisine">Mediterranean cuisines</a> like <a href="/wiki/Maghrebi_cuisine" title="Maghrebi cuisine">Maghrebi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_cuisine" title="Turkish cuisine">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_cuisine" title="Italian cuisine">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern_cuisine" title="Middle Eastern cuisine">Middle Eastern cuisine</a>, and modern fusion food restaurants can all be found in Jakarta.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium,_Asia_Cup_2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium%2C_Asia_Cup_2007.jpg/220px-Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium%2C_Asia_Cup_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium%2C_Asia_Cup_2007.jpg/330px-Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium%2C_Asia_Cup_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium%2C_Asia_Cup_2007.jpg/440px-Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium%2C_Asia_Cup_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium,_Asia_Cup_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> match at Gelora Bung Karno Stadium</div></div></div>
<p>Jakarta hosted the <a href="/wiki/1962_Asian_Games" title="1962 Asian Games">1962 Asian Games</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHanna1962193â203_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanna1962193â203-165">[165]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2018_Asian_Games" title="2018 Asian Games">2018 Asian Games</a>, co-hosted by <a href="/wiki/Palembang" title="Palembang">Palembang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Jakarta also hosted the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_Games" title="Southeast Asian Games">Southeast Asian Games</a> in 1979, 1987, 1997 and 2011 (supporting <a href="/wiki/Palembang" title="Palembang">Palembang</a>). <a href="/wiki/Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium" title="Gelora Bung Karno Stadium">Gelora Bung Karno Stadium</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> hosted the group stage, quarterfinal and final of the <a href="/wiki/2007_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2007 AFC Asian Cup">2007 AFC Asian Cup</a> along with Malaysia, Thailand and Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> The largest capacity retractable roof stadium in Asia <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_International_Stadium" title="Jakarta International Stadium">JIS</a> is located at <a href="/wiki/Tanjung_Priok" title="Tanjung Priok">Tanjung Priok</a> district, completed in 2022.
</p><p>The Senayan sports complex has several sports venues, including the Bung Karno football stadium, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madya_Stadium" title="Madya Stadium">Madya Stadium</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Istora_Senayan" title="Istora Senayan">Istora Senayan</a>, aquatic arena, baseball field, basketball hall, a shooting range, several indoor and outdoor tennis courts. The Senayan complex was built in 1960 to accommodate the 1962 Asian Games. For basketball, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kelapa_Gading_Sport_Mall" title="Kelapa Gading Sport Mall">Kelapa Gading Sport Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kelapa_Gading" title="Kelapa Gading">Kelapa Gading</a>, North Jakarta, with a capacity of 7,000 seats, is the home arena of the Indonesian national basketball team. <a href="/wiki/The_BritAma_Arena" title="The BritAma Arena">The BritAma Arena</a> serves as a playground for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Satria_Muda_Pertamina_Jakarta" title="Satria Muda Pertamina Jakarta">Satria Muda Pertamina Jakarta</a>, the 2017 runner-up of the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Basketball_League" title="Indonesian Basketball League">Indonesian Basketball League</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_International_Velodrome" title="Jakarta International Velodrome">Jakarta International Velodrome</a> is a sporting facility located at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rawamangun" title="Rawamangun">Rawamangun</a>, which was used as a venue for the <a href="/wiki/2018_Asian_Games" title="2018 Asian Games">2018 Asian Games</a>. It has a seating capacity of 3,500 for <a href="/wiki/Track_cycling" title="Track cycling">track cycling</a>, and up to 8,500 for shows and concerts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> which can also be used for various sports activities such as volleyball, badminton and futsal. <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_International_Equestrian_Park" title="Jakarta International Equestrian Park">Jakarta International Equestrian Park</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> sports venue located at <a href="/wiki/Pulo_Gadung" title="Pulo Gadung">Pulomas</a>, which was also used as a venue for <a href="/wiki/2018_Asian_Games" title="2018 Asian Games">2018 Asian Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asian_Games_2018_GBK_Stadium_Opening_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3088" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Asian_Games_2018_GBK_Stadium_Opening_01.jpg/250px-Asian_Games_2018_GBK_Stadium_Opening_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Asian_Games_2018_GBK_Stadium_Opening_01.jpg/375px-Asian_Games_2018_GBK_Stadium_Opening_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Asian_Games_2018_GBK_Stadium_Opening_01.jpg/500px-Asian_Games_2018_GBK_Stadium_Opening_01.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Asian_Games_2018_GBK_Stadium_Opening_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Games_2018" title="Asian Games 2018">Asian Games 2018</a> opening ceremony in Gelora Bung Karno Stadium, 2018</div></div></div>
<p>The Jakarta <a href="/wiki/Car-Free_Days" title="Car-Free Days">Car-Free Days</a> are held weekly on Sunday on the main avenues of the city, Jalan Sudirman, and Jalan Thamrin, from 6 AM to 11 AM. The briefer Car-Free Day, which lasts from 6 AM to 9 AM, is held on every other Sunday. The event invites local pedestrians to do sports and exercise and have their activities on the streets that are usually full of traffic. Along the road from the Senayan traffic circle on Jalan Sudirman, South Jakarta, to the "Selamat Datang" Monument at the Hotel Indonesia traffic circle on Jalan Thamrin, north to the National Monument in Central Jakarta, cars are blocked from entering. During the event, morning gymnastics, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Callisthenics" title="Callisthenics">callisthenics</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aerobic_exercises" title="Aerobic exercises">aerobic exercises</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> <a href="/wiki/Game" title="Game">games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jogging" title="Jogging">jogging</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycling" title="Bicycling">bicycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skateboarding" title="Skateboarding">skateboarding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Badminton" title="Badminton">badminton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a>, on-street library and musical performances take over the roads and the main parks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jakarta's most popular home football club is <a href="/wiki/Persija_Jakarta" title="Persija Jakarta">Persija</a>, which plays in <a href="/wiki/Liga_1_(Indonesia)" title="Liga 1 (Indonesia)">Indonesia Super League</a>. Another football team in Jakarta is <a href="/wiki/Persitara_Jakarta_Utara" title="Persitara Jakarta Utara">Persitara</a> who compete in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liga_Indonesia_Premier_Division" title="Liga Indonesia Premier Division">2nd Division Football League</a> and play in <a href="/wiki/Kamal_Muara_Stadium" title="Kamal Muara Stadium">Kamal Muara Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soemantri_Brodjonegoro_Stadium" title="Soemantri Brodjonegoro Stadium">Soemantri Brodjonegoro Stadium</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Marathon" title="Jakarta Marathon">Jakarta Marathon</a> each November is recognised by <a href="/wiki/Association_of_International_Marathons_and_Distance_Races" title="Association of International Marathons and Distance Races">AIMS</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Athletic_Association_Federation" title="International Athletic Association Federation">IAAF</a>. It was established in 2013. It brings <a href="/wiki/Sports_tourism" title="Sports tourism">sports tourism</a>. In 2015, more than 15,000 runners from 53 countries participated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jakarta successfully hosted the first <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_ePrix" title="Jakarta ePrix">Jakarta ePrix</a> race of the <a href="/wiki/Formula_E" title="Formula E">Formula E</a> championship in June 2022 at <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_International_e-Prix_Circuit" title="Jakarta International e-Prix Circuit">Ancol Circuit</a>, North Jakarta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_entertainment">Media and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Media and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TVRITower.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2027" data-file-width="1410" decoding="async" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/TVRITower.jpg/170px-TVRITower.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/TVRITower.jpg/255px-TVRITower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/TVRITower.jpg/340px-TVRITower.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TVRITower.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main TV tower of <a href="/wiki/TVRI" title="TVRI">TVRI</a> at its headquarters in Jakarta</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Indonesia" title="List of newspapers in Indonesia">List of newspapers in Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_Jakarta" title="List of radio stations in Jakarta">List of radio stations in Jakarta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_stations_in_Indonesia" title="List of television stations in Indonesia">List of television stations in Indonesia</a></div>
<p>Jakarta is home to most of Indonesian national newspapers, besides some local-based newspapers. Daily local newspapers in Jakarta are <i><a href="/wiki/Pos_Kota" title="Pos Kota">Pos Kota</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warta_Kota" title="Warta Kota">Warta Kota</a></i>, as well as the now-defunct <i><a href="/wiki/Indopos" title="Indopos">Indopos</a></i>. National newspapers based in Jakarta include <i><a href="/wiki/Kompas" title="Kompas">Kompas</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Koran_Tempo" title="Koran Tempo">Koran Tempo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Media_Indonesia" title="Media Indonesia">Media Indonesia</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Republika_(Indonesian_newspaper)" title="Republika (Indonesian newspaper)">Republika</a></i>, most of them has a news segment covering the city. A bunch of business newspapers (<i><a href="/wiki/Bisnis_Indonesia" title="Bisnis Indonesia">Bisnis Indonesia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Investor_Daily" title="Investor Daily">Investor Daily</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Kontan" title="Kontan">Kontan</a></i>) and sports newspapers (<i><a href="/wiki/TopSkor" title="TopSkor">TopSkor</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tribun_Network" title="Tribun Network">Super Ball</a></i>) are also published.
</p><p>Newspapers other than in Indonesian, mainly for a national and global audience, are also published daily. Examples are English-language newspapers <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jakarta_Post" title="The Jakarta Post">The Jakarta Post</a></i> and online-only <i><a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Globe" title="Jakarta Globe">The Jakarta Globe</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese language</a> newspapers also circulate, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Indonesia_Shang_Bao" title="Indonesia Shang Bao">Indonesia Shang Bao</a></i> (å°å°¼åæ¥), <i><a href="/wiki/Harian_Indonesia" title="Harian Indonesia">Harian Indonesia</a></i> (å°å°¼ææ´²æ¥æ¥), and <i><a href="/wiki/International_Daily_News" title="International Daily News">Guo Ji Ri Bao</a></i> (å½éæ¥æ¥). The only <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese language</a> newspaper is <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Jakarta_Shimbun" title="The Daily Jakarta Shimbun">The Daily Jakarta Shimbun</a></i> (ãããããæ°è).
</p><p>Around 75 radio stations broadcast in Jakarta, 52 on the <a href="/wiki/Frequency_modulation" title="Frequency modulation">FM</a> band, and 23 on the <a href="/wiki/Amplitude_modulation" title="Amplitude modulation">AM</a> band. Radio entities are based in Jakarta, for example, national radio networks <a href="/wiki/MNC_Trijaya_FM" title="MNC Trijaya FM">MNC Trijaya FM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prambors_FM" title="Prambors FM">Prambors FM</a>, Trax FM, I-Radio, Hard Rock FM, Delta FM, Global FM  and the public radio <a href="/wiki/Radio_Republik_Indonesia" title="Radio Republik Indonesia">RRI</a>; as well as local stations <a href="/wiki/Gen_98.7_FM" title="Gen 98.7 FM">Gen FM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Elshinta" title="Radio Elshinta">Radio Elshinta</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Z99,9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Z99,9 (page does not exist)">Z99,9</a>.
</p><p>Jakarta is the headquarters for Indonesia's public television <a href="/wiki/TVRI" title="TVRI">TVRI</a> as well as private national television networks, such as <a href="/wiki/Metro_TV_(Indonesian_TV_network)" title="Metro TV (Indonesian TV network)">Metro TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/TvOne_(Indonesian_TV_network)" title="TvOne (Indonesian TV network)">tvOne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kompas_TV" title="Kompas TV">Kompas TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/RCTI" title="RCTI">RCTI</a> and <a href="/wiki/NET_(Indonesian_TV_network)" title="NET (Indonesian TV network)">NET</a>. Jakarta has local television channels such as <a href="/wiki/TVRI_Jakarta" title="TVRI Jakarta">TVRI Jakarta</a>, <a href="/wiki/JakTV" title="JakTV">JakTV</a>, Elshinta TV and KTV. Many TV stations are analogue <a href="/wiki/PAL" title="PAL">PAL</a>, but some are now converting to digital signals using <a href="/wiki/DVB-T2" title="DVB-T2">DVB-T2</a> following a <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial_television_in_Indonesia" title="Digital terrestrial television in Indonesia">government plan to digital television migration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Jakarta" title="Governor of Jakarta">Governor of Jakarta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Istana_Merdeka.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Istana_Merdeka.jpg/220px-Istana_Merdeka.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Istana_Merdeka.jpg/330px-Istana_Merdeka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Istana_Merdeka.jpg/440px-Istana_Merdeka.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Istana_Merdeka.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jakarta <a href="/wiki/Merdeka_Palace" title="Merdeka Palace">Merdeka Palace</a></div></div></div>
<p>Jakarta is administratively equal to a <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">province</a> with special status. The executive branch is headed by an elected <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Jakarta" title="Governor of Jakarta">governor</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Vice_Governor_of_Jakarta" title="Vice Governor of Jakarta">vice governor</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Regional_People%27s_Representative_Council" title="Jakarta Regional People's Representative Council">Jakarta Regional People's Representative Council</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <i lang="id">Dewan Perwakilan Rakyat Daerah Provinsi Daerah Khusus Ibukota Jakarta</i>, DPRD DKI Jakarta) is the legislative branch with 106 directly elected members. The <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_City_Hall" title="Jakarta City Hall">Jakarta City Hall</a> at the south of <a href="/wiki/Merdeka_Square,_Jakarta" title="Merdeka Square, Jakarta">Merdeka Square</a> houses the office of the governor and the vice governor, and serves the main administrative office.
</p><p>Executive governance consists of five administrative cities (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <i lang="id">Kota Administrasi</i>), each headed by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> and one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regencies_of_Indonesia" title="Regencies of Indonesia">administrative regency</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <i lang="id">Kabupaten Administrasi</i>) headed by a <a href="/wiki/Regent" title="Regent">regent</a> (<i>bupati</i>). Unlike other cities and regencies in Indonesia where the mayor or regent are directly elected, Jakarta's mayors and regents are chosen by the governor. Each city and regency is divided into administrative districts.
</p><p>Aside from representatives to the provincial parliament, Jakarta sends 21 delegates to the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Representative_Council" title="People's Representative Council">national lower house parliament</a>. The representatives are elected from Jakarta's three national electoral districts, which also includes overseas voters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> It also sends 4 delegates, just like other provinces, to the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Representative_Council" title="Regional Representative Council">national upper house parliament</a>.
</p><p>The Jakarta Smart City (JSC) program was launched on 14 December 2014 with a goal for smart governance, smart people, smart mobility, smart economy, smart living and a smart environment in the city using the web and various smartphone-based apps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_safety">Public safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Public safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Jakarta_Metropolitan_Regional_Police" title="Greater Jakarta Metropolitan Regional Police">Greater Jakarta Metropolitan Regional Police</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <i lang="id">Polda Metro Jaya</i>) is the police force that is responsible to maintain law, security, and order for the <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_metropolitan_area" title="Jakarta metropolitan area">Jakarta metropolitan area</a>. It is led by a two-star police general (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inspector_General_of_Police#Indonesia" title="Inspector General of Police">Inspector General of Police</a>) with the title of "Greater Jakarta Regional Police Chief" (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <i lang="id">Kepala Kepolisian Daerah Metro Jaya</i>, abbreviated <span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Kapolda Metro Jaya</i></span>). Its office is located at Jl. Jenderal Sudirman Kav. 55, Senayan, Kebayoran Baru, South Jakarta and their hotline-emergency number is 110.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kodam_Jaya" title="Kodam Jaya">Jayakarta Military Regional Command</a> (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <i lang="id">Komando Daerah Militer Jayakarta</i>, abbreviated <span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Kodam Jaya</i></span>) is the territorial army of the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Army" title="Indonesian Army">Indonesian Army</a>, which serves as a defence component for Jakarta and its surrounding areas (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Jakarta" title="Greater Jakarta">Greater Jakarta</a>). It is led by an army <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_General" title="Major General">Major General</a> with the title of "Jakarta Military Regional Commander" (<a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>: <i lang="id">Panglima Daerah Militer Kodam Jaya</i>, abbreviated <span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Pangdam Jaya</i></span>). The Jakarta Military Command is located at <a href="/wiki/East_Jakarta" title="East Jakarta">East Jakarta</a> and oversees several military battalions ready for defending the capital city and its vital installations. It also assists the Jakarta Metropolitan Police during certain tasks, such as supporting security during <a href="/wiki/State_visit" title="State visit">state visits</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VVIP" title="VVIP">VVIP</a> security, and <a href="/wiki/Riot_control" title="Riot control">riot control</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_finances">Municipal finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Municipal finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Jakarta provincial government relies on transfers from the central government for the bulk of its income. Local (non-central government) sources of revenue are incomes from various taxes such as vehicle ownership and vehicle transfer fees, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The ability of the regional government to respond to Jakarta's many problems is constrained by limited finances.
</p><p>The provincial government consistently runs a surplus of between 15 and 20% of planned spending, primarily because of delays in procurement and other inefficiencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Regular under-spending is a matter of public comment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> In 2013, the budget was around Rp 50Â trillion ($US5.2Â billion), equivalent to around $US380 per citizen. Spending priorities were on education, transport, flood control, environment and social spending (such as health and housing).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> Jakarta's regional budget (APBD) was Rp 77.1Â trillion ($US5.92Â billion), Rp 83.2Â trillion ($US6.2Â billion), and Rp 89Â trillion ($US6.35Â billion) for the year of 2017, 2018 and 2019 respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Special_Capital_Region_of_Jakarta.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8858" data-file-width="8858" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Special_Capital_Region_of_Jakarta.png/220px-Special_Capital_Region_of_Jakarta.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Special_Capital_Region_of_Jakarta.png/330px-Special_Capital_Region_of_Jakarta.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Special_Capital_Region_of_Jakarta.png/440px-Special_Capital_Region_of_Jakarta.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Special_Capital_Region_of_Jakarta.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the administrative cities (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Kota administratif</i></span>) in Jakarta province. The Thousand Islands Regency (to the north) is not shown. Each administrative city is further divided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Indonesia" title="Districts of Indonesia">districts</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kecamatan" title="Kecamatan">Kecamatan</a></i>).</div></div></div>
<p>Jakarta consists of five <i>Kota Administratif</i> (Administrative cities/municipalities), each headed by a mayor, and one <i>Kabupaten Administratif</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regencies_of_Indonesia" title="Regencies of Indonesia">Administrative regency</a>). Each city and regency is divided into districts/Kecamatan. The administrative cities/municipalities of Jakarta are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Central_Jakarta" title="Central Jakarta">Central Jakarta</a> (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Jakarta Pusat</i></span>) is Jakarta's smallest city and the administrative and political centre. It is divided into eight districts. It is characterised by large parks and Dutch colonial buildings. Landmarks include the National Monument (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monas" title="Monas">Monas</a>), <a href="/wiki/Istiqlal_Mosque,_Jakarta" title="Istiqlal Mosque, Jakarta">Istiqlal Mosque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Cathedral" title="Jakarta Cathedral">Jakarta Cathedral</a> and museums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Jakarta" title="West Jakarta">West Jakarta</a> (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Jakarta Barat</i></span>) has the city's highest concentration of small-scale industries. It has eight districts. The area includes Jakarta's Chinatown and Dutch colonial landmarks such as the Chinese Langgam building and <a href="/wiki/Toko_Merah" title="Toko Merah">Toko Merah</a>. It contains part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jakarta_Old_Town" title="Jakarta Old Town">Jakarta Old Town</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_Jakarta" title="South Jakarta">South Jakarta</a> (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Jakarta Selatan</i></span>), originally planned as a satellite city, is now the location of upscale shopping centres and affluent residential areas. It has ten districts and functions as Jakarta's <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a> buffer,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> but recently the green belt areas are threatened by new developments. Much of the <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a> is concentrated in Kebayoran Baru, Setiabudi, a small part in Tebet, Pancoran, &amp; Mampang Prapatan, bordering the Tanah Abang/Sudirman area of Central Jakarta. The area is known as the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Triangle_of_Jakarta" title="Golden Triangle of Jakarta">Jakarta Golden Triangle</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/East_Jakarta" title="East Jakarta">East Jakarta</a> (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Jakarta Timur</i></span>) territory is characterised by several industrial sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Also located in East Jakarta are <a href="/wiki/Taman_Mini_Indonesia_Indah" title="Taman Mini Indonesia Indah">Taman Mini Indonesia Indah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Halim_Perdanakusuma_International_Airport" title="Halim Perdanakusuma International Airport">Halim Perdanakusuma International Airport</a>. This city has ten districts.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/North_Jakarta" title="North Jakarta">North Jakarta</a> (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Jakarta Utara</i></span>) is bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Java_Sea" title="Java Sea">Java Sea</a>. It is the location of <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Tanjung_Priok" title="Port of Tanjung Priok">Port of Tanjung Priok</a>. Large- and medium-scale industries are concentrated there. It contains part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jakarta_Old_Town" title="Jakarta Old Town">Jakarta Old Town</a>, which was the centre of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">VOC</a> trade activity during the colonial era. Also located in North Jakarta is <a href="/wiki/Ancol_Dreamland" title="Ancol Dreamland">Ancol Dreamland</a> (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Taman Impian Jaya Ancol</i></span>), the largest integrated tourism area in Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> North Jakarta is divided into six districts.</li></ul>
<p>The only administrative regency (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">kabupaten</i></span>) of Jakarta is the <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Islands_(Indonesia)" title="Thousand Islands (Indonesia)">Thousand Islands</a> (<span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Kepulauan Seribu</i></span>), formerly a <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Indonesia" title="Districts of Indonesia">district</a> within North Jakarta. It is a collection of 105 small islands located on the Java Sea. It is of high conservation value because of its unique ecosystems. Marine tourism, such as diving, water bicycling, and windsurfing, are the primary tourist activities in this territory. The main mode of transportation between the islands is speed boats or small ferries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Roads_of_Jakarta" title="Category:Roads of Jakarta">Category:Roads of Jakarta</a></div>

Airport Rail Link">Airport Railink</a></div></div></div></div>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Jakarta" title="Transport in Jakarta">Transport in Jakarta</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Transport_in_Jakarta&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jalan_MH_Thamrin_Menteng,_Jakarta_Pusat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4096" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Jalan_MH_Thamrin_Menteng%2C_Jakarta_Pusat.jpg/220px-Jalan_MH_Thamrin_Menteng%2C_Jakarta_Pusat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Jalan_MH_Thamrin_Menteng%2C_Jakarta_Pusat.jpg/330px-Jalan_MH_Thamrin_Menteng%2C_Jakarta_Pusat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Jalan_MH_Thamrin_Menteng%2C_Jakarta_Pusat.jpg/440px-Jalan_MH_Thamrin_Menteng%2C_Jakarta_Pusat.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jalan_MH_Thamrin_Menteng,_Jakarta_Pusat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>MH Thamrin Street area, Gondangdia, Menteng, Central Jakarta</div></div></div>
<p>As a metropolitan area of about 30 million people, Jakarta has a variety of transport systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Transport_in_Jakarta_NYT8413_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Transport_in_Jakarta_NYT8413-198">[198]</a></sup> Jakarta was awarded 2021 global <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Transport_Award" title="Sustainable Transport Award">Sustainable Transport Award</a> (STA) for integrated public transportation system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city prioritized development of road networks, which were mostly designed to accommodate private vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Transport_in_Jakarta_Easts.info_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-Transport_in_Jakarta_Easts.info-200">[200]</a></sup> A notable feature of Jakarta's present road system is the <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">toll road</a> network. Composed of an <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Inner_Ring_Road" title="Jakarta Inner Ring Road">inner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_Outer_Ring_Road" title="Jakarta Outer Ring Road">outer</a> <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">ring road</a> and five toll roads radiating outwards, the network provides inner as well as outer city connections. An 'odd-even' policy limits road use to cars with either odd or even-numbered registration plates on a particular day as a transitional measure to alleviate traffic congestion until the future introduction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_road_pricing" title="Electronic road pricing">electronic road pricing</a>.
</p><p>There are many bus terminals in the city, from where buses operate on numerous routes to connect neighborhoods within the city limit, to other areas of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jabodetabek" title="Jabodetabek">Greater Jakarta</a> area and to cities across the island of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>. The biggest of the bus terminal is <a href="/wiki/Pulo_Gebang_Bus_Terminal" title="Pulo Gebang Bus Terminal">Pulo Gebang Bus Terminal</a>, which is arguably the largest of its kind in Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Transport_in_Jakarta_bisnis.liputan6.com_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-Transport_in_Jakarta_bisnis.liputan6.com-201">[201]</a></sup> Main terminus for long distance train services are <a href="/wiki/Gambir_railway_station" title="Gambir railway station">Gambir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pasar_Senen_railway_station" title="Pasar Senen railway station">Pasar Senen</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Indonesia" title="High-speed rail in Indonesia">High-speed railways</a> being constructed connecting Jakarta to <a href="/wiki/Bandung" title="Bandung">Bandung</a> and another one is at planning stage from Jakarta to <a href="/wiki/Surabaya" title="Surabaya">Surabaya</a>.
</p><p>Rapid transit in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Jakarta" title="Greater Jakarta">Greater Jakarta</a> consists of <a href="/wiki/TransJakarta" title="TransJakarta">TransJakarta</a> bus rapid transit, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_LRT" title="Jakarta LRT">Jakarta LRT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta_MRT" title="Jakarta MRT">Jakarta MRT</a>, <a href="/wiki/KRL_Commuterline" title="KRL Commuterline">Greater Jakarta Commuter Rail</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soekarno-Hatta_Airport_Rail_Link" title="Soekarno-Hatta Airport Rail Link">Soekarno-Hatta Airport Rail Link</a>. Another transit system <a href="/wiki/Greater_Jakarta_LRT" title="Greater Jakarta LRT">Greater Jakarta LRT</a> is expected to be operational by 2022. The city administration is building transit oriented development like <a href="/wiki/Dukuh_Atas_TOD" title="Dukuh Atas TOD">Dukuh Atas TOD</a> and <a href="/wiki/CSW-ASEAN_TOD" title="CSW-ASEAN TOD">CSW-ASEAN TOD</a> in several area across Jakarta to facilitate commuters to transfer between different mode of public transportation.
</p><p>Privately owned bus systems like <a href="/wiki/Kopaja" title="Kopaja">Kopaja</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MetroMini,_Jakarta" title="MetroMini, Jakarta">MetroMini</a>, <a class="extiw" href="https://id.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayasari_Bakti" title="id:Mayasari Bakti">Mayasari Bakti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pengangkutan_Penumpang_Djakarta" title="Pengangkutan Penumpang Djakarta">PPD</a> also provide important services for Jakarta commuters with numerous routes throughout the city. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedicab" title="Pedicab">Pedicabs</a> are banned from the city for causing traffic congestion. <a href="/wiki/Auto_rickshaw#Indonesia" title="Auto rickshaw">Bajaj</a> auto rickshaw provide local transportation in the back streets of some parts of the city. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angkot" title="Angkot">Angkot</a> microbuses also play a major role in road transport of Jakarta. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">Taxicabs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_taxi#Indonesia" title="Motorcycle taxi">ojeks</a> (motorcycle taxis) are available in the city.
</p><p>The city administration has undertaken a project to build about 500 kilometers of <a href="/wiki/Bicycle" title="Bicycle">bicycle</a> lanes. As of June 2021, Jakarta already has 63 kilometers of bicycle lanes, and another 101 kilometers will be added by the end of the year 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Soekarno%E2%80%93Hatta_International_Airport" title="SoekarnoâHatta International Airport">SoekarnoâHatta International Airport</a> (CGK) is the main <a href="/wiki/Airport" title="Airport">airport</a> serving the Greater Jakarta area, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halim_Perdanakusuma_Airport" title="Halim Perdanakusuma Airport">Halim Perdanakusuma Airport</a> (HLP) accommodates private and <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost</a> <a href="/wiki/Domestic_flight" title="Domestic flight">domestic flights</a>. Other airports in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jabodetabek" title="Jabodetabek">Jakarta metropolitan area</a> include <a href="/wiki/Pondok_Cabe_Airport" title="Pondok Cabe Airport">Pondok Cabe Airport</a> and an airfield on Pulau Panjang, part of the <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Islands_(Indonesia)" title="Thousand Islands (Indonesia)">Thousand Island archipelago</a>.
</p>
Indonesia's busiest and Jakarta's main seaport <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Tanjung_Priok" title="Port of Tanjung Priok">Tanjung Priok</a> serves many ferry connections to different parts of Indonesia. The old port <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kelapa" title="Sunda Kelapa">Sunda Kelapa</a> only accommodate <a href="/wiki/Pinisi" title="Pinisi">pinisi</a>, a traditional two-masted wooden sailing ship serving inter-island freight service in the archipelago. <a href="/wiki/Muara_Angke" title="Muara Angke">Muara Angke</a> is used as a public port to <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Islands_(Indonesia)" title="Thousand Islands (Indonesia)">Thousand Islands (Indonesia)</a>, while Marina <a href="/wiki/Ancol" title="Ancol">Ancol</a> is used as a tourist port.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></div></div>
<p>Jakarta is part of the Maritime <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> that runs from the Chinese coast via the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> to the Mediterranean and there to the Upper Adriatic region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Batavia_1897.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1467" data-file-width="926" decoding="async" height="349" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Batavia_1897.jpg/220px-Batavia_1897.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Batavia_1897.jpg/330px-Batavia_1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Batavia_1897.jpg/440px-Batavia_1897.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Batavia_1897.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Batavia map of Meester Cornelis (now <a href="/wiki/Jatinegara" title="Jatinegara">Jatinegara</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>To transform the city into a more livable one, a ten-year <i>urban regeneration</i> project was undertaken, for Rp 571Â trillion ($40.5Â billion). The project aimed to develop infrastructure, including the creation of a better integrated public transit system and the improvement of the city's clean water and wastewater systems, housing and flood control systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jakarta has many of the country's best-equipped private and public <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Indonesia" title="Healthcare in Indonesia">healthcare facilities</a>. In 2012, Governor of Jakarta <a href="/wiki/Joko_Widodo" title="Joko Widodo">Joko Widodo</a> introduced a <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> program, the 'Healthy Jakarta Card' (<i>Kartu Jakarta Sehat</i>, KJS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> In January 2014, the Indonesian government launched a universal health care system called the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaminan_Kesehatan_Nasional" title="Jaminan Kesehatan Nasional">Jaminan Kesehatan Nasional</a></i> (JKN), which is run by <a href="/wiki/BPJS_Kesehatan" title="BPJS Kesehatan">BPJS Kesehatan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBritnell201547_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBritnell201547-210">[210]</a></sup> KJS is being integrated into JKN,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> and KJS cards are still valid as of 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> As of 2021, 85.55% of the people of Jakarta is covered by JKN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>Government-run hospitals are of a good standard but are often overcrowded. Government-run specialised hospitals include <a href="/wiki/Dr._Cipto_Mangunkusumo_Hospital" title="Dr. Cipto Mangunkusumo Hospital">Dr. Cipto Mangunkusumo Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gatot_Soebroto_Army_Hospital" title="Gatot Soebroto Army Hospital">Gatot Soebroto Army Hospital</a>, as well as community hospitals and <a href="/wiki/Puskesmas" title="Puskesmas">puskesmas</a>. Other options for healthcare services include private hospitals and clinics. The private healthcare sector has seen significant changes, as the government began allowing foreign investment in the private sector in 2010. While some private facilities are run by nonprofit or religious organisations, most are for-profit. Hospital chains such as <a href="/wiki/Siloam_Hospitals" title="Siloam Hospitals">Siloam</a>, Pondok Indah Hospital Group, Mayapada, Mitra Keluarga, Medika, Medistra, Ciputra, and Hermina operate in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply">Water supply</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Water supply">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Water_privatisation_in_Jakarta" title="Water privatisation in Jakarta">Water privatisation in Jakarta</a></div>
<p>Two private companies, PALYJA and Aetra, provide piped water in the western and eastern half of Jakarta respectively under 25-year concession contracts signed in 1998. A public asset holding company called PAM Jaya owns the infrastructure. Eighty per cent of the water distributed in Jakarta comes through the West Tarum Canal system from Jatiluhur reservoir on the <a href="/wiki/Citarum_River" title="Citarum River">Citarum River</a>, 70Â km (43Â mi) southeast of the city. The water supply was privatised by President Suharto in 1998 to the French company <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suez_Environnement" title="Suez Environnement">Suez Environnement</a> and the British company <a href="/wiki/Thames_Water" title="Thames Water">Thames Water</a> International. Both companies subsequently sold their concessions to Indonesian companies. Customer growth in the first seven years of the concessions had been lower than before, possibly because of substantial inflation-adjusted tariff increases during this period. In 2005, tariffs were frozen, leading the private water companies to cut down on investments.
</p><p>According to PALYJA, the service coverage ratio increased substantially from 34% (1998) to 65% (2010) in its western half of the concession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> According to data by the Jakarta Water Supply Regulatory Body, access in the eastern half of the city served by PTJ increased from about 57% in 1998 to about 67% in 2004 but stagnated afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> However, other sources cite much lower access figures for piped water supply to houses, excluding access provided through public hydrants: one study estimated access as low as 25% in 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> while another estimated it to be as low as 18.5% in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> Those without access to piped water get water mostly from wells that are often salty and unsanitary. As of 2017, according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Energy_and_Mineral_Resources_(Indonesia)" title="Ministry of Energy and Mineral Resources (Indonesia)">Ministry of Energy and Mineral Resources</a>, Jakarta had a crisis over clean water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_embassies_in_Jakarta" title="List of embassies in Jakarta">List of embassies in Jakarta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ASEAN_HQ_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1811" data-file-width="2551" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/ASEAN_HQ_1.jpg/220px-ASEAN_HQ_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/ASEAN_HQ_1.jpg/330px-ASEAN_HQ_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/ASEAN_HQ_1.jpg/440px-ASEAN_HQ_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ASEAN_HQ_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Secretariat of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">ASEAN</a> at Jl. Sisingamangaraja No.70A, <a href="/wiki/South_Jakarta" title="South Jakarta">South Jakarta</a>, Indonesia</div></div></div>
<p>Jakarta hosts foreign <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_mission" title="Diplomatic mission">embassies</a>. Jakarta also serves as the seat of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> (ASEAN) Secretariat and is ASEAN's diplomatic capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jakarta is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Network_of_Major_Cities_21" title="Asian Network of Major Cities 21">Asian Network of Major Cities 21</a>, <a href="/wiki/C40_Cities_Climate_Leadership_Group" title="C40 Cities Climate Leadership Group">C40 Cities Climate Leadership Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Smart_Cities_Network" title="ASEAN Smart Cities Network">ASEAN Smart Cities Network</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_â_sister_cities">Twin towns â sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Twin towns â sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Street_Tripoli_Libya.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3472" data-file-width="2604" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Jakarta_Street_Tripoli_Libya.JPG/170px-Jakarta_Street_Tripoli_Libya.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Jakarta_Street_Tripoli_Libya.JPG/255px-Jakarta_Street_Tripoli_Libya.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Jakarta_Street_Tripoli_Libya.JPG/340px-Jakarta_Street_Tripoli_Libya.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Street_Tripoli_Libya.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jakarta Street in <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Indonesia" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Indonesia">List of twin towns and sister cities in Indonesia</a></div>
<p>Jakarta signed <a href="/wiki/Sister_city" title="Sister city">sister city</a> agreements with other cities, including <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a>. To promote friendship between the two cities, the main avenue famous for its shopping and business centres was named after Jakarta's Moroccan sister city. No street in Casablanca is named after Jakarta. However, the Moroccan capital city of Rabat has an avenue named after <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>, Indonesia's first president, to commemorate his visit in 1960 and as a token of friendship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JakartaPost2_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-JakartaPost2-222">[222]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jakarta's sister cities are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sisters_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-sisters-223">[223]</a></sup>
</p>

<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco"><img alt="Morocco" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/23px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/35px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/45px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a>, Morocco</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine"><img alt="State of Palestine" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="216" data-file-width="432" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Palestine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Palestine.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Palestine.svg/35px-Flag_of_Palestine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Palestine.svg/46px-Flag_of_Palestine.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/East_Jerusalem" title="East Jerusalem">East Jerusalem</a>, Palestine</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam"><img alt="Vietnam" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/23px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/35px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/45px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a>, Vietnam</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_and_friendship">Cooperation and friendship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jakarta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cooperation and friendship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jakarta has established a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, especially on integrated urban water management, including capacity-building and knowledge exchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NESO_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-NESO-225">[225]</a></sup> This cooperation is mainly because both cities are dealing with similar problems; they lie in low-lying flat plains and are prone to flooding. Additionally, they have both implemented drainage systems involving canals, dams, and pumps vital for both cities for below-sea-level areas.
</p><p>In addition to its sister cities, Jakarta cooperates with:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sisters_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-sisters-223">[223]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, United States</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary"><img alt="Hungary" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/46px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, Hungary</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia"><img alt="Australia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, Australia</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, France</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands"><img alt="Netherlands" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, Netherlands</li></ul>
